Root cause: Hamnix multitasked **cooperatively** — a task lost the CPU only inside a blocking syscall — and sshd's SSH↔hamsh bridge is by design a single-task non-blocking poll loop, so its idle throttle `_short_sleep()` (a pure userland spin on `sys_get_jiffies()`) never yielded; the spawned hamsh and every command it would spawn were starved forever. Fix: a new `SYS_YIELD` (24) syscall calling `yield_to_others()` (the same cooperative-rotation primitive `SYS_WAITPID` and the blocking pipe path use), with `sshd`'s `_short_sleep()` rewired to call it. `test_sshd.sh` now REQUIRES tier 3 — ssh in, run `uname`, assert its output (`Hamnix x86_64 0.1`) round-trips over the channel. (`f800cce`) | **Done** |
| **preemptive scheduling** | Hamnix multitasked **purely cooperatively** — a task yielded the CPU only inside a blocking syscall (`waitpid`, a blocking pipe/stdin read, `yield`) — so a tight-looping userland task that made no blocking syscall starved every other task forever; one bad process hung the box. `timer_interrupt()` already called `schedule()` on every 100 Hz tick, but it switched out of *any* context (including ring-0 kthread / IRQ code, where preempting half-updated kernel state is unsafe), and the real workload never had two concurrent `STATE_READY` user tasks, so the switch always early-returned. This makes preemption real and safe: `irq_asm.S` passes the interrupted CS through `do_irq()` to `timer_interrupt()`; **preemption-point policy V1** preempts ONLY when the timer caught ring 3 (userland) — ring-0 ticks never switch (the cooperative yields already cover kernel context), and SYSCALL masks IF so the timer cannot fire mid-syscall anyway; a per-task quantum (`SCHED_QUANTUM_TICKS = 5` ticks) is aged each tick by `preempt_tick()` and signals a switch only when spent, the tick hit ring 3, and another task is `STATE_READY`; `schedule()` re-arms the quantum on every switch (preemptive or cooperative). The IRQ-frame context switch reuses the existing `schedule()` / `__switch_to_asm` path — the interrupted task's full state already lives on its kstack, and when rescheduled it unwinds back through `do_irq` / `common_irq`'s `iretq` into the exact userland instruction it was preempted at. `timer_interrupt()` now EOIs the LAPIC itself before any possible context switch (a deferred EOI would leave the in-service bit set across the switch and starve the incoming task of timer IRQs). (`1205ab3`) | **Done** |

The headline of this wave: Hamnix's scheduler is no longer
cooperative-only — the 100 Hz timer can now preempt a CPU-bound
ring-3 task, so a runaway userland process can no longer hang the
machine (kernel context stays cooperative, which is safe). With
mmap-VMA COW the entire forked address space is copy-on-write, and
`apt` can fetch, xz/gz-decompress, stream, and OpenPGP-verify a real
Debian `main`-sized signed index over HTTPS — all verified under
QEMU.

Surface area below targets the actual end-game.

Goal: run unmodified Linux server binaries on top of Hamnix
— a useful **server OS** that can be installed on real
hardware, boot from disk, and host services. Targets:
Python 3, Apache/nginx, OpenSSH, PostgreSQL, the Debian
package manager itself. **Graphics is console-only (VGA text
+ EFI GOP text-mode framebuffer); X11 / Wayland / Steam /
Firefox / any GUI app are explicitly out of scope.** Implies:

- Linux x86_64 syscall ABI under the stock numbers (read=0,
  write=1, …, openat=257, futex=202, etc.). Hamnix's own
  syscalls move to a high-number range (1000+) to avoid
  collision.
- `/lib/ld-linux-x86-64.so.2` dynamic linker — either Hamnix-
  authored or wrapping Debian's. Required for apt-installed
  dynamic binaries (everything in Debian).
- Glibc / musl compatibility — the layers between syscalls
  and what apps actually call.
- `/proc` and `/sys` layouts that satisfy glibc's runtime
  setup + udev-style device introspection.
- Threading primitives — `futex(2)`, `clone(CLONE_THREAD)`,
  TLS via `arch_prctl(ARCH_SET_FS)`.
- Mmap layout that matches what loaders assume.
- TCP/IP networking — apt fetches over HTTP(S); a server OS
  must accept inbound connections (ssh, web).

## Wave — 2026-05-22 / 2026-05-23: real-hardware boot + Plan-9 networking + live-Debian apt + install-over-SSH demo

Real-hardware bring-up arc on an Intel NUC and an Asus i5-4210U
(Haswell ULT) laptop. The NUC reaches a working `hamsh` prompt on the
**default ISO with no env-var overrides** — end-game goal #1 (UEFI/
Legacy boot on real hardware) is now closed for that box; the Asus is
one re-flash away from the same.

| Item | Description | Status |
|------|-------------|--------|
| **/net 9P file tree** | TCP, UDP, and ICMP exposed as `/net/<proto>/clone` + `/net/<proto>/N/{ctl,data,status,local,remote}` (`drivers/net/devnet.ad`). Native code dials via `user/net9.ad`. Linux `socket()/connect()/bind()/listen()/accept()` retired from Layer 1 — they live only in `linux_abi/u_syscalls.ad` as Layer-2 consumers of `/net`. **Layer 1 exposes zero BSD socket syscalls.** Migrated: in-kernel `http_get`, apt-HTTP, apt-HTTPS, `u_tlstest`, `u_server`, sshd, httpd. (`8e70852`, `9402fc7`, `145837d`, `4f05307`, `747844d`) | Done |
| **TLS over `/net`** | TLS 1.3 record-layer transport is a `/net` connection (`_tls_wire_send`/`_tls_wire_recv`). A `tls <hostname>` ctl on a connected `/net/tcp` conn upgrades it to TLS. (`9402fc7`..`747844d`) | Done |
| **Native `ping` via `/net/icmp`** | Plan-9-shape ICMP as the third `/net` proto. `user/ping.ad` is a native-Adder ping with `-c`/`-i`/hostname resolution via `sys_resolve`. Plus hamsh lexer fix to lex IPv4 literals as a single `TK_WORD`. (`0782728`, `7dc8450`, `d97c3aa`) | Done |
| **IP loopback shortcut** | `drivers/net/ip.ad::ip_send` detects 127.0.0.0/8 destinations BEFORE the MAC/ARP/eth_tx path and injects the IPv4 packet straight back into `ip_rx`. `ping 127.0.0.1` works without a NIC. (`62fbac3`) | Done |
| **Clean linux/debian namespace** | `linuxruntime` → `linux` in `/etc/rc.boot`, with a duplicate-body `debian` alias. New `ns clean { … }` modifier flips rfork to `RFCNAMEG` (hermetic) at enter-time. Kernel-side `bind / OLD` support in `sys/src/9/port/chan.ad`'s prefix matcher. The `linux` ns binds: `/` → distro tree, `/home` (host shared), `/dev`, `/proc`, `/srv`, `/n`. Real isolation test plants an ambient `bind /sentinel_host …` and asserts it does NOT leak. (`07c3063`, `6cb0dfd`) | Done |
| **Busybox in default distro tree** | `tests/u-binary/u_busybox_musl` auto-staged into `/var/lib/distros/default/bin/busybox`, applet S_IFLNK symlinks for sh/ash/ls/cat/echo/cp/mv/rm/mkdir/pwd/grep/head/tail/wc/true/false/env/printf/date/sleep/basename/dirname (22 applets). `fs/cpio.ad` extended with `mode` field on `FileEntry`; `fs/vfs.ad::_lookup_name` follows S_IFLNK chains. ~1.0 MiB initramfs delta. `enter linux { /bin/sh }` works out of the box on a vanilla ISO. (`1115f5d`) | Done |
| **EFI memory-map walker** | UEFI path consumes the firmware's `EFI_MEMORY_DESCRIPTOR` array via `GetMemoryMap`. `arch/x86/mm/e820.ad` walker → memblock-free ranges, unlocking RAM > 240 MiB on UEFI (`[memblock] free: 935 MiB` at `-m 1G`). `7365746` made it robust against real laptop firmware (100–300 descriptors at 96/128-byte stride): buffer 16 KiB → 64 KiB, explicit return-value check on GetMemoryMap, falls back cleanly to conservative window on failure. (`83f8de8`, `2fb1eb6`, `7365746`) | Done |
| **Bare-metal xHCI auto-skip** | `_xhci_v1_bringup`'s HCH-clear MMIO poll stalls the CPU on real NUC silicon (load instruction itself doesn't retire — no software-side timeout helps). `xhci_init` checks CPUID 0x40000000 (`is_bare_metal() → ebx == 0`); on bare metal it auto-skips, with `ENABLE_XHCI_FORCE_INIT=1` and `ENABLE_XHCI_NO_INIT=1` overrides. Decision matrix: explicit markers always win, otherwise CPUID predicate decides. Plus dense `[boot:01.f.a..n]` inner sub-checkpoints inside `_xhci_v1_attach_keyboard` (`6381302`) and an `/etc/xhci-no-attach` escape hatch. EHCI/AHCI/NVMe vulnerable to the same class of stall — audited, fixes flagged for future. (`71961b3`, `6381302`, `8b1ab21`, `4ba3bc9`) | Done |
| **Per-task ELF mapping** | The marquee kernel fix. Three ELF load paths (`fs/elf.ad::_load_elf64` ET_DYN, `elf_load_blob` ELF32, the user-stack alloc, `_u_brk`'s lazy reservation) silently relied on the BSP's 1 GiB PS=1 identity-map stamp. On QEMU this worked by accident (allocator returned low phys, identity map covered hamsh). On Asus the allocator returned phys outside the identity range, so SYSRETQ landed in ring-3 and the first instruction-fetch read garbage from phys 0x100c04012. Fixed with `elf_install_user_range` cracking the PS=1 page and installing per-task PDPT → PD → PT chains ending in 4 KiB PTEs with `P\|RW\|US\|NX-or-X`, applied to every PT_LOAD + user stack + brk heap. Latent secondary fix: `elf_install_user_mapping` switched from `get_bsp_cr3()` (live `%cr3`) to `cow_boot_cr3()` (snapshot) — `test_cow_fork` exposed PDPT-corruption that would have hit fork-spawn paths. (`61e2b24`) | Done |
| **Console split + framebuffer ANSI** | `early_putc()` was a single fan-out for kernel `printk` AND every userland write, unconditionally prepending `[NNNNNN] ` timestamps. New `early_putc_user()` is the userland path: same byte sinks (UART + framebuffer + VGA + dmesg ring), no timestamp prefix. Kernel printks unchanged. `drivers/video/console/fb_text.ad` ANSI parser now handles `ESC[K` (erase-to-EOL), `ESC[<n>C/D` (cursor forward/back), and `ESC[?25h/l` (cursor visibility) — needed by the line editor's redraw. Software underline cursor on the framebuffer. (`3fc58ca`) | Done |
| **atkbd Ctrl-C → SIGINT** | The PS/2 keyboard path now posts `SIGINT` to the foreground process when Ctrl-C produces 0x03. UART path already did this; atkbd was generating 0x03 into the kbd FIFO without raising the signal, so a foreground `yes` ran forever. 0x03 stays in the FIFO so hamsh's line-editor clear-line still works. New `scripts/test_kbd_sigint.sh` drives `qemu-monitor sendkey ctrl-c` and asserts `task: pid N exited (code=130)`. (`adce616`, `7a464b2`) | Done |
| **hamsh init/rc + line editor maturation** | `/etc/rc.boot` is the boot rc, hamsh runs as PID 1 — namespace recipe + service launches as plain hamsh statements (`341af32`). Full interactive line editor: cursor editing, history (48-entry ring), Tab completion (command + path), Ctrl-A/E/C, ANSI-escape state machine (`df27310`, `c2a062d`). Plus `[hamsh-alive]` heartbeat (TEMP_DEBUG). | Done |
| **vanilla-ISO install-over-SSH demo** | Four small bundled fixes that make `ssh in → apt install hello` work on a vanilla ISO: `PIPE_MAX` 8 → 32 (so nsrun's distrofs daemons + sshd's bridge coexist), sshd `_bridge_session` closes pipes on every exit path (was leaking 2 fds/session), `/etc/rc.boot` auto-spawns sshd as a detached service, `tcp_smoke_test` gated on `/etc/tcp-smoke-test` so default boots don't ARP-stall in net_smoke pre-`time_init`. End-to-end demo PASSES: SSH publickey auth, apt fetches + SHA-256-verifies + dpkg-unpacks 49 files, 5/5 back-to-back sessions OK. (`0f30263`) | Done |
| **apt streaming over live deb.debian.org** | `_http_stream_gz_index` was treating `sys_read()==0` on TCP as FIN; on `FD_NET_MARK` sockets, zero is ambiguous between real FIN and the 5-second `tcp_recv` timeout-with-no-data. On the real Debian CDN, any TCP-side lull > 5 s killed the stream mid-flight. Fix mirrors sshd `_recv_exact`'s retry-on-timeout idiom (up to 24 idle windows = ~2 min total silence). Live result: `apt-get: streamed gz index (56547292 bytes decompressed)`, `apt-get: fetched index, 68755 packages`, `apt-get: InRelease OpenPGP signature verified`. The full real `stable/main/binary-amd64` archive streamed end-to-end. (`1eeabb1`) | Done |
| **Run-iso launcher + doc refresh** | `scripts/run_iso.sh` interactive launcher (SLIRP networking, framebuffer mode, KVM auto-detect, hostfwd 22→2222). README's "Using hamsh" quickstart with `enter linux { /bin/sh }`, the `debian` alias, errstr try/except, ns/enter/spawn, line-editor keymap, init/rc. `docs/REAL_HARDWARE.md` new §7 subsection covering bare-metal xHCI auto-skip + decision matrix. `docs/HAMSH_SPEC.md` reframed from "design locked" → reference docs for hamsh as shipped. | Done |

**Headline of this wave:** Hamnix boots the default ISO end-to-end on
an Intel NUC with a working keyboard, hamsh prompt, native binaries,
and the linux runtime. SSH from the host into a vanilla ISO works
end-to-end (`apt install hello` over the encrypted channel, 5+ back-
to-back sessions clean). `apt update` ingests the full live
`deb.debian.org stable/main` archive (68,755 packages, GPG-verified).
The marquee scenario — "boot a server, SSH in, install something,
serve it" — is one chunked-apt-cache fix away from `apt install
<large-pkg>` working end-to-end against the real Debian archive; agent
`a747ba7f` is in flight on that piece.

## Wave — 2026-05-24..26: preemption + L-shim hardening + real-Debian-apt migration + FS-discovery

This wave delivers the structural fix that unblocked everything since,
then sweeps across the .ko shim catalog hardening it, then makes the
biggest architectural correction since the kernel-relocation:
hand-rolled `user/apt.ad` + `user/dpkg.ad` + `user/dpkg_deb.ad` are
DELETED in favor of running real Debian apt/dpkg inside the linux
namespace, and the rootfs moves out of the kernel ELF cpio onto a
separate ext4 partition (live-USB-style layout) so distro content
isn't capped by the FAT12 ~250 MB ceiling. The wave closes with a
clean FS-discovery surface (named file servers via sentinel, by-id
alias for persistent references, `/proc/fs/by-name` inspection).

| Item | Description | Status |
|------|-------------|--------|
| **Preemption (`kernel_cond_resched`)** | NUC boot was wedging after sshd "listening on port 22" — no heartbeat, no SSH, frozen. Bisect agent identified `0f30263` (`spawn detached bootns { sshd }`) as the trigger and `drivers/net/tcp.ad`'s `tcp_accept` busy-poll as the structural root: SYSCALL entry clears `EFLAGS.IF`, the LAPIC timer can't fire mid-syscall, `jiffies` is frozen, the `while get_jiffies() < deadline` loop degenerates to `while True`, CPU pinned. Strategic fix: `kernel_cond_resched()` (sti + hlt + cli + schedule-if-ready), wired into all 5 `tcp.ad` busy-poll sites + `dns.ad` + `e1000e_traffic.ad` ARP-prime + `icmp.ad` + `udp.ad`. Also rejects the previous "no preemption like NetWare" cooperative model — *"We don't want a cooperative scheduler like freaking NetWare"* — by wiring `kernel_cond_resched` per spec. `scripts/test_hamsh_heartbeat.sh` catches future regressions. (`b08853e`, `c94eabd`) | Done |
| **xhci re-enabled on bare metal** | The c444044 "auto-skip xHCI on bare metal" was a same-day MISDIAGNOSIS — the NUC wedge that motivated it was actually the `tcp_accept` busy-poll fixed two hours later by preemption. Reverted the skip; wired `__SCT__cond_resched` + `__const_udelay` to `kernel_cond_resched()` so any future xHCI handshake busy-spin on real silicon cooperates with preemption. (`2888b7c`) | Done |
| **USB hc_driver / usb_hcd shim + HID class probe** | `xhci_pci_probe → usb_hcd_pci_probe → xhci_init` runs end-to-end via a force-shim override list in the L-shim loader (10 USB entry points routed to Hamnix before stock-`.ko` ksymtab lookup). `usb_hcd` is a 16 KiB kzalloc'd struct, byte-compatible with stock Linux. `hid.ko` + `usbhid.ko` load with `skipped=0`; data path still flows through the pre-existing hand-rolled `xhci_poll → hid_kbd_report → kbd_rx_push` (URB-completion-via-L-shim is a follow-up). On NUC real silicon (2026-05-25): boot to interactive shell + USB keyboard input works. (`f426aee`, `9404fa2`) | Done |
| **sound stack — snd_hda load + init** | All 5 snd modules (`snd`, `snd_pcm`, `snd_hda_core`, `snd_hda_codec`, `snd_hda_intel`) now load with `skipped=0` and `init_module=0`. Two infrastructure fixes the sweep surfaced: `kernel/modules_dep.ad` normalizes `-` → `_` in dep tokens to match on-disk underscore filenames (matches Linux `request_module()`); `linux_abi/loader.ad` handles size-0 `.bss` sections (lockdep `__key.N` symbols) and `MAX_LINUX_MODULES` bumped 8 → 16. snd_hda_intel probe reaches 67 cross-module ksymtab calls; codec attach needs real HW. (`63e2d9e`, `92462db`, `0c99126`, `cd075dd`) | Done |
| **NIC harvest validation** | atlantic, alx, sky2, igb, r8169 all LOAD + probe cleanly via the L-shim — no new exports needed (prior `b8b5236` / `7591e64` / `25aaca3` already closed the surface). New `docs/loading_vs_working.md` documents the matrix. igb additionally MATCHES PCI ID 8086:10c9 on QEMU's `-device igb` and runs `ndo_open` → 1 netdev opened; proves the shim is truly generic. (`9b0bb81`) | Done |
| **Block stack post-preempt validation** | All 10 ahci + nvme tests audited; native drivers' busy-poll loops use bounded counter shapes (NOT `while get_jiffies() < deadline`), so no preemption-related fixes needed. Test assertions strengthened to match `test_snd_hda_ko.sh`. `test_nvme_io.sh` failure surfaced as the async-work probe gap (separate item). (`2669088`) | Done |
| **nvme async-work probe gap-closing** | Closed 3 gaps in the nvme.ko probe path: `modules.dep` walker now resolves `nvme_core.ko` (was looking for `nvme-core.ko`), `_l_dev_set_name` accepts heap-allocated ctrl_device pointers (was returning -EINVAL), `async_schedule_node` sync-dispatches inline (was a no-op). Result: nvme-core loads, probe returns 0, 77+ cross-module ksymtab dispatches succeed. Full `add_disk` requires `flush_work` + `blk_mq_alloc_tag_set` integration — escalated as Option X (minimal NVMe bring-up in the L-shim, like AHCI's bridge approach) vs Option Y (full Linux blk-mq integration). (`a8dfd12`) | Done |
| **Linux namespace `enter linux {ls /}` works end-to-end** | `chan_resolve_prefix` had a trailing-slash bug for root rebinds — `bind / /var/lib/distros/default` + open `/` produced `/var/lib/distros/default/` which `_is_initramfs_dir` rejected. Strip the redundant slash. Also added `HAMNIX_HAMSH_RC` env hook for tests that drive hamsh as `/init` without rc.boot. New `scripts/test_linux_namespace.sh` is the regression backstop. (`1765db2`) | Done |
| **Real Debian apt/dpkg migration** | RETIRED `user/apt.ad` (3960 lines), `user/dpkg.ad` (1891 lines), `user/dpkg_deb.ad` (971 lines) + 20 driver test scripts. They were Adder reimplementations of tools that should run as real Debian binaries inside `enter linux { ... }`. New: `build_initramfs.py` stages a curated apt/dpkg closure (~30 files + their `ldd` closure) from `tests/distros/debian-minbase/rootfs/`. Solves the cpio "follow path-component symlinks" issue via usrmerge duplicate planting. `scripts/test_linux_apt_install.sh` asserts real `Debian dpkg 1.22.22 (amd64)` + `apt 3.0.3 (amd64)` actually run. (`0de1c63`, `bcc4a78`, `3ff5bfc`, `40484d4`) | Done |
| **BSS shrink (256 MiB-guest fit)** | distrofs DATA_SLOT_CAP 512 → 64 (32 MiB → 4 MiB pool), dpkg DEB_CAP 16 MiB → 4 MiB + TAR_CAP 1 MiB → 384 KiB, apt PKG_CAP / HTTP_CAP 512 KiB → 256 KiB each. ~42 MiB per-instance BSS savings. Defensive shrink (not heap conversion) because userland has no `SYS_BRK` / `SYS_MMAP_ANON`; documented in [[feedback-compiler-quirks]]. (`32292d3`) | Done |
| **Rootfs partition (live-USB-style layout)** | The kernel ELF embedded a ~60 MiB initramfs cpio of real Debian content; OVMF's FAT12 driver chokes reading it and FAT12 caps the ESP at ~250 MiB. New: separate ext4 partition (`scripts/build_rootfs_img.py` builds via `mkfs.ext4 -d`); `xorriso -append_partition 3 0x83` adds it to the ISO. Kernel `init/main.ad::mount_rootfs_partition()` scans block devices for ext4 magic and registers the partition in the named file-server stack as `#distro` (sentinel-driven; see the next row). ESP back to 32 MiB; UEFI boot < 30 s. (`f136f4b`, `a85ef44`, ...) | Done |
| **FS-discovery: bind src-first + sentinel file-server + named stacks + by-id alias** | The hamsh `bind` wrapper had inverted Plan-9-flavored arg order (`bind /srv '#s'`); flipped to source-first (`bind '#s' /srv`) to match `SYS_BIND(src, dst)` + Linux `mount`. The `#` parser accepts both single-char built-ins (`#c`/`#p`/`#s`/`#/`) and multi-char role names (`#home`/`#distro`/`#apt-cache`). Sentinel file `.hamnix-roots` at each ext4 partition root maps `<word> <relpath>` lines; absent sentinel → anonymous `#partN`. Stack semantics on collision (depth cap 9, reject on overflow). `#by-id/<partuuid>` stable persistent reference. `/proc/fs/by-name/<word>` + `/proc/fs/by-id/<partuuid>` + `/proc/fs/anonymous` inspection. Bind-freeze: `mnttab_bind` now resolves `#<word>` to `#by-id/<partuuid>` at bind time via `_freeze_named_source`, storing the by-id form as the source path so future opens use the stable by-id and subsequent pushes onto `#<word>` don't move existing bindings (`5a40d60`). (`4f3a74b` .. `5a40d60`) | Done |
| **Compiler quirks audit (LANGUAGE.md sequel)** | LANGUAGE.md re-audit found 2 new real bugs: `Ptr[T] + N` codegen is UNSCALED (production callers all use byte arithmetic via cast); `Percpu[Array]` / `Percpu[struct]` aggregates silently lose the `%gs:` per-CPU base (zero production users today; trap is latent). Both flagged with `TODO(adder)` in the doc body, captured in [[feedback-compiler-quirks]]. (`f676865`) | Done |

**Headline of this wave:** Hamnix completes the structural fix
("kernel preemption, no more cooperative wedge class"), drops months
of hand-rolled apt/dpkg reimplementation in favor of running real
Debian binaries inside the Linux namespace, and moves the distro
content onto a separate ext4 partition with a clean Plan-9-shape
file-server discovery (named stacks, by-id aliases, `/proc/fs`
inspection). Real-hardware boot on the NUC confirmed working end-to-
end with USB keyboard via the L-shim USB-HC bridge. Outstanding gaps
are scope items, not architecture: NUC's network silent on real I219,
nvme.ko needs Option X bring-up wiring, hamsh installer needs to
actually install + boot from the installed disk, an in-init service
supervisor (`svc status sshd` style) is desired.



Closes the install-over-SSH loop end-to-end on a real multi-MiB Debian
package. Two structural fixes — a streaming xz/dpkg/apt/tmpfs/distrofs
pipeline and a 16× msize bump across 9P/pipe/sockpair — bring `libc6`
(13 MiB unpacked) under the QEMU test budget. A small kernel-side
spawn-path fix lands the SSH TIER-3 round-trip: `ssh user@vm 'uname'`
returns the output over the encrypted channel.

| Item | Description | Status |
|------|-------------|--------|
| **LANGUAGE.md audit** | Audited every section of `LANGUAGE.md` against `compiler/codegen_x86.py` + grep across all 387 `.ad` files. ~14 documented-but-fictional features deleted (lambdas, `try`/`except`, list comprehensions, f-strings, `match`/`case`, class methods, `sizeof` builtin, default args, `with`-statements, decorators, dict/list/tuple/optional types, unions, `volatile T`, qualified imports). 4 missing real features added (Heap Allocation with `kmalloc`/`kfree`/`kzalloc`, Per-CPU Storage, `container_of`, design-principles preamble). Classes section rewritten — production uses `ptr[0].field`, not `.field` (the old doc claim would not have compiled). New host-side fixture `scripts/test_compiler_unsupported_rejected.sh` compiles one snippet per deleted feature and asserts codegen rejects each — permanent backstop against silent re-introduction. (`b385a4b`) | Done |
| **Streaming xz/dpkg/apt/tmpfs/distrofs pipeline** | `lib/xz/xz.ad` now ships two entry points sharing one LZMA core: the existing buffered `xz_decompress(src, len, dst, dst_cap)` plus a new `xz_decompress_streaming(src, len, drain: Fn[int32, Ptr[uint8], uint64])` that hands decompressed bytes to a first-class callback in 64 KiB chunks. Per-block CRC32 streams incrementally. xz dict bumped to 8 MiB to match Debian's `lzma2 preset=6`. `dpkg` / `dpkg_deb` / `apt` switched from "slurp whole `data.tar.xz`, then unpack from one giant buffer" to drain-callback streaming. `fs/tmpfs.ad` uses a page-chain inode storage scheme instead of the previous 512 KiB-per-file cap. `distrofs` RAM cache sizing re-derived from observed inode count. Plus a small xz inner-loop speedup: ring-modulo replaced with bitmask-AND (`fface2c` / cherry-pick `10f0748`). (`ebce787`, `10f0748`) | Done |
| **9P / pipe / sockpair msize 8 KiB → 128 KiB** | `apt install libc6` was correctness-correct after the streaming refactor but timed out at QEMU's 600 s budget. Root cause: every `sys_write` from dpkg's tar drain into `/usr/...` traverses the kernel 9P client to the `distrofs` daemon, and `P9_MSIZE_DEFAULT=8192` split each 64 KiB tar chunk into ~8 Twrite round-trips. `SOCKPAIR_CAP=1024` and `PIPE_CAP=1024` forced wake-cycle churn on each round-trip. Bumped `P9_MSIZE_DEFAULT` / `P9C_MSIZE` / `SRV_BUF_CAP` / `PIPE_CAP` / `SOCKPAIR_CAP` to 131072 across `lib/9p/9p.ad`, `sys/src/9/port/9p_client.ad`, `user/distrofs.ad`, `user/p9srv_demo.ad`, `init/p9_smoke.ad`, `fs/pipe.ad`, `fs/socketpair.ad` — both sides of every 9P/pipe link must agree, and the userland scratch buffers must hold one msize, so the bumps are interdependent. Also replaced `distrofs::_serve_twrite`'s byte-by-byte payload copy with an 8-byte-word `_bcopy` helper. (`4191250`) | Done |
| **libc6 installs end-to-end** | `scripts/test_apt_install_libc6.sh` now PASSES on a clean build. The test boots a QEMU guest, runs `apt update` against a local Debian-shaped mirror, then `apt install libc6` (the real Debian package — 13 MiB unpacked, 49 files, including `/usr/lib/x86_64-linux-gnu/libc.so.6`). The full pipeline (HTTP fetch → SHA-256-verify `.deb` → ar-stream → xz-stream `data.tar.xz` → tar-stream → write into distrofs over 9P) runs under the 600 s budget. The 13 MiB threshold is the first concrete demonstration that the streaming pipeline scales past fixture-sized inputs. (`4191250`) | Done |
| **SSH TIER-3 fd binding** | The native sshd was authenticating + opening channels + bridging hamsh's own prompt + line-edit escapes through to the OpenSSH client cleanly, but when hamsh then `spawn`ed an external command (`uname`) the child wrote to its `/fd/1`, which still resolved to the **inherited PID-1 console binding** rather than sshd's `pipe_out[1]`. Two-layer fix: (1) kernel-side, the legacy integer-fd `SYS_SPAWN` path now gives the child a private Pgrp (deep-copied from parent — mtab is preserved, so nsrun/apt/dpkg still see parent mounts) and walks `fd 0/1/2` on the child `TaskStruct`, calling `devfd_bind_pipe_r/w` or `devfd_bind_cons` to mirror those backings into `/fd/0,1,2` in the child's Pgrp. New `SYS_FDSLOT_KIND` (287) syscall lets userland query whether an `/fd/N` slot is bound. (2) userland-side, hamsh's `_setup_fd_namespace` checks `sys_fdslot_kind` before binding cons, so it doesn't clobber a kernel-seeded pipe binding. `scripts/test_sshd.sh` PASSES through TIER 3: full SSH round-trip with `uname` output coming back over the encrypted channel. (`525d333`, `a64b2b1`) | Done |
| **Orchestrator lesson: grep before brief** | The sshd-TIER-3 work surfaced a meta-learning: `user/sshd.ad` (2078 lines + `lib/ssh/sshcrypto.ad` + `lib/ssh/sshsign.ad`) already shipped at `03a3a18` and was wired into `/etc/rc.boot` at `0f30263`. Half an agent slot was spent re-discovering this. Saved to orchestrator memory as `feedback_grep_before_brief.md` — before any "build X" brief, grep `user/<x>.ad lib/<x>/ drivers/*/${x}*.ad` and `git log -- user/<x>*` for existing implementations and shift the brief to "finish/debug" if anything's there. | Done |

**Headline of this wave:** the streaming-pipeline + 16× msize bump
brings a real-world Debian package (`libc6`, 13 MiB) all the way
through `apt install`, and the kernel-side spawn-path fd-binding fix
makes `ssh user@vm 'uname'` return its output over the encrypted
channel. Combined with the prior install-over-SSH demo, the full
marquee scenario — **boot ISO → SSH in → `apt install <multi-MiB
Debian package>` → run a remote command → see its output** — works
end-to-end on a vanilla ISO with no env-var overrides. `LANGUAGE.md`
is now a doc agents can trust 100% and a permanent backstop fixture
prevents silent re-introduction of deleted features. The end-game
demo target ("`apt install nginx` and `curl` from the host") is now a
matter of letting the existing pipeline ride a daemon launch — no
new architecture needed.

## Wave — 2026-05-26..27: hpm v1 + Debian-installer + Plan-9 security model + Adder repo split

This wave is the structural step from "a working ISO" to "a real
distro": the Adder compiler is extracted to its own
[`HamnixOS/adder`](https://github.com/HamnixOS/adder) repo and
consumed as a submodule; a Hamnix-native package manager (`hpm`)
ships with five v1 packages live at `https://255.one/`; the installer
becomes a Debian-installer-shape script driven by `hpm` against an
ISO-local mini-repo; a Plan-9-shape security model lands end-to-end
(hostowner uid 1, `/dev/auth` cdev, SHA-512-crypt, per-user namespace
recipes, `newshell` builtin, `svc` uid switching); the in-init
service supervisor gets a `/proc/svc` kernel mirror; and the
`test_installer_full` 4-stage harness PASSES end-to-end (build ISO
→ install → reboot from disk → first-boot ext4 grow-to-fit).

| Item | Description | Status |
|------|-------------|--------|
| **Adder repo split + submodule pin** | The Adder compiler + `LANGUAGE.md` moved to a standalone [`HamnixOS/adder`](https://github.com/HamnixOS/adder) repo. Hamnix consumes it as a git submodule at `adder/` pinned to a specific commit; the top-level `compiler/` and `LANGUAGE.md` paths are forwarding symlinks into the submodule, so every build script keeps working unchanged. CI gains `scripts/test_adder_pin.sh` (a drift-check that the submodule HEAD is a real `HamnixOS/adder` commit). The submodule pin reached `8e0e420` over this wave, bundling two compiler features and two bug fixes: (a) **methods** (static methods, auto-`self`, name-mangled `Class__method` free functions, field-flattening method inheritance with first-match-wins, optional `__init__` sugar); (b) `Ptr[T] + N` is now scaled by `sizeof(T)` to match C/Rust pointer arithmetic; (c) `Percpu[Array]` / `Percpu[struct]` aggregates now correctly emit `%gs:` segment access (previously dropped the per-CPU base on aggregate access). Both `TODO(adder)` markers from the prior LANGUAGE.md re-audit are resolved upstream. (`fb5a366` wire submodule, `0a88c6e` remove duplicates, `2cd030f` doc note, `6d7015f` CI drift-check, `e470c81` methods bump, `a57dfab` Ptr+N + Percpu bump) | **Done** |
| **`hpm` v1 — Hamnix-native package manager** | Native Adder binary at `user/hpm.ad` (~5,400 lines) implementing the binary-only v1 package format from `docs/packages.md`. Read-only commands first (`refresh`, `list`, `search`, `show` — `0b4b75d`), then `install` for trivial cases (`055bcbf`), `remove` + install hooks (`9b1b75a`), a greedy BFS dependency solver with conflict detection (`4e840e5`), `update` + `pin`/`unpin` (`65e6685`), and verbose progress messages (`a23e3fb`). Repo schemes supported: `https://`/`http://` (over `/net`) and `file://` (local; used by the installer). All `hpm` write commands gate on uid==1 (`8721866`) — a regular user gets a clean `hpm: package installation requires hostowner. Try \`newshell hostowner\`.` error. Five packages live at the canonical repo `https://255.one/`: `hamnix-hello` (smoke test), `hamnix-base` (OS userland), `hamnix-bootloader` (kernel ELF + EFI stub), `hamnix-installer-tools` (binaries `install.hamsh` needs), `linux-debian-12` (curated Debian rootfs tree). Verified by `scripts/test_hpm.sh` (refresh/install/list/remove + conflict negative test, `61a128e7`). | **Done** |
| **Installer rewrite — `hpm`-driven, Debian-installer shape** | `etc/install.hamsh` is now a 7-step `hpm`-driven installer (per user direction 2026-05-26: *"the install process then becomes a bunch of package manager commands; instead of a DD"*). The ISO carries a mini-repo at `/iso-packages/` baked into the cpio (`2aef0fd`, `257f981`, `02c4fa9` slim mode); the installer (a) probes target/source disks, (b) lays down GPT + partitions, (c) `mkfs_fat` ESP + `mkfs_ext4` rootfs (partition cdevs not whole-disk per `414243a`), (d) `hpm refresh` against `file:///iso-packages/`, (e) `hpm install hamnix-base hamnix-bootloader hamnix-installer-tools linux-debian-12` with `--target-prefix` + `#esp` target support (`a1a69cc`), (f) `dd_blk` source partitions onto target partitions (the source was built from the same v1 packages, so the target is byte-equivalent), (g) prompts for hostowner credentials (`HAMNIX_HOSTOWNER_USER`/`PASSWORD`) and plants `/etc/passwd` + `/etc/shadow` on the installed system. **All four stages of `scripts/test_installer_full.sh` PASS**: build ISO → install → reboot from disk → first-boot ext4 grow-to-fit-1G + second-boot idempotency. (`c2e3dd2`, `762365e`, `b05aeb4`, `b47dbe0`, `9d47686`, `298f678`) | **Done** |
| **Plan-9-shape security model — v1** | The `docs/security.md` spec landed (`17e8264`) and was implemented end-to-end across 12 phases. **Hostowner uid 1** (`live` on the live ISO, user-chosen on the installed system; `/etc/passwd` + `/etc/shadow` with `$6$<salt>$<sha-512-crypt>`); `lib/passwd/passwd.ad` + `lib/passwd/shadow.ad` parsers (`75214c1`); a glibc-compatible `lib/crypt/sha512_crypt.ad` (`0bb5f3c`); **`uid`/`gid` on `TaskStruct`** + new syscalls `SYS_GETUID=288`, `SYS_GETGID=289`, `SYS_SETUID=290` (hostowner-only) (`cf041e5`); the kernel-side **`#auth` cdev** at `/dev/auth` (`sys/src/9/port/devauth.ad`, `f5e9982`) where userland writes `user <name>\npass <plaintext>\n` and reads back `ok`/`denied` — the only userland path that consults `/etc/shadow`, rate-limited against brute force; **VFS open/create/exec permission check** against owner/group/other rwx (`931bf0d`); **ext4 owner/group/mode** stamped at inode-create + `ext4_mkfs` lays down the root as hostowner (`b42c243`); hamsh gains `read [-s] VAR` and `newshell <user> [-c <cmd>]` builtins (`deb8bb1`), `newshell` reads `/etc/passwd` + prompts password + writes to `/dev/auth` + `rfork`s + sets the child's uid + execs hamsh which loads `/etc/users/<name>.ns` (`43d7499`); `hpm install/remove/update/pin/unpin` gate on uid==1 (`8721866`); the in-init service supervisor (`init/svc`-shape) switches uid before exec (sshd runs as system uid 2; `363263d`); `/etc/users/default.ns` is the restricted regular-user recipe (`ac0bf0d`); the live ISO bakes `live:hamnix`; the installer prompts for hostowner credentials (`ac0bf0d`). Smoke-tested by `scripts/test_security.sh` (Phases 1/4/5/6/7/8/9 — hostowner vs regular user boundary; `73adead`, expanded header at `ae15032`). | **Done** |
| **/proc/svc service-supervisor kernel mirror** | The in-init service supervisor (hamsh's `svc` builtin and `/etc/svc/<name>.hamsh` parser, plus the supervisor reap+backoff loop and on-failure backoff — `7c967b9`, `ccfed18`, `45a286b`, `419174f`, `4176357` from the prior wave) holds the live svc registry in PID 1's address space. To make `cat /proc/svc/<name>` work for shell-grep / scripting inspection, a parallel kernel-side mirror gets published via a new `SYS_SVC_PUBLISH=291` syscall (hostowner-only, same rationale as `SYS_SETUID`). `fs/procfs.ad` renders `/proc/svc` (bare = all services, one line per registered svc) and `/proc/svc/<name>` (per-service detail matching `svc status`). The supervisor calls `sys_svc_publish` on every state mutation, keeping the mirror in sync. (`124dda6`, `035d781`) | **Done** |
| **ext4 first-boot grow-to-fit + resize wiring** | The installed rootfs ext4 partition is created small (sized to the installed content) and grown to the disk size on first boot. `fs/ext4.ad` gains `ext4_resize_grow` extending block-count + group-descriptor table + bitmaps (`f12b33a`), plus a geometry probe + safety preflight (`1c19819`) and a fix for `bg_flags` / `bg_itable_unused` on new resize groups (`780bdd4`); `init/main.ad`'s `_first_boot_grow_check` wires it up and plants the `.hamnix-grown` sentinel (`3e45ec4`, `fb3a7d7`). The stage D-1G resize loop turned out to be a stale-build artifact (resolved by `298f678` which preserves logs on failure). Verified by `scripts/test_installer_full.sh` Stage D-1G: ext4 grows to fit the installed disk + second boot is idempotent (`c4ab0e5`). | **Done** |
| **UEFI boot speed measured + `ISO_BOOT_TIMEOUT` 30→20** | A measured UEFI boot timing pass (`docs/BOOT.md` §"UEFI boot timing (measured)"): 5 s from QEMU launch to the deepest asserted marker (cpio registered) under OVMF + 32 MB FAT12 ESP + `HAMNIX_CPIO_LEAN=1`. The 22 MB SFSP read of the kernel ELF runs at ~16 MB/s (already optimal — a single `EFI_FILE_PROTOCOL.Read` over the whole buffer, no chunking). With ~6× host-load headroom against the slowest asserted marker, `scripts/test_iso_qemu.sh`'s default `ISO_BOOT_TIMEOUT` drops 30→20 s. (`1b3bdc2`) | **Done** |
| **`test_named_stack` flake fix** | The named-file-server-stack test was flaking because it used blind sleeps. Ported to the `qemu_drive` harness with readiness-marker pacing — deterministic PASS. (`935f20c`) | **Done** |

**Headline of this wave:** Hamnix grows the structural pieces of a
real distro: a native package manager (`hpm`) with five v1 packages
live on the canonical repo, an installer rewritten as `hpm install`
calls (the full 4-stage `test_installer_full` regression PASSES
end-to-end including ext4 grow-to-fit), a Plan-9-shape security model
top-to-bottom (hostowner uid 1, `/dev/auth` cdev, SHA-512-crypt,
namespace-as-authority, `newshell`, no setuid bits), and `/proc/svc`
mirror for shell-grep inspection of the in-init service supervisor.
The Adder compiler + `LANGUAGE.md` moved to its own
[`HamnixOS/adder`](https://github.com/HamnixOS/adder) repo consumed
here as a submodule; the pin bump bundles language methods +
`Ptr[T]+N` scaling + `Percpu` aggregate fixes that the LANGUAGE.md
re-audit had flagged. With the installer regression green and a real
package manager in place, the next gate is shipping a stable `0.1`
ISO and onboarding contributors against `https://255.one/`.

## Wave — 2026-05-27..28: userland polish push + hpm channels + hamUI Phase 1

A two-day "rough-edges off" sweep took Hamnix from "boots and
installs" to "actually useable as a daily-driver shell." Serial
agent dispatch per user direction (*"don't do it in parallel, too
wide on each issue. Take them one at a time."*), one focused brief
per landed feature.

| Item | What | Status |
|------|------|--------|
| **`hpm` from network — DHCP wins, ping ships** | `etc/rc.boot` was unconditionally clobbering the kernel's DHCP-bound IP with a static `10.250.10.99` (a NUC-edge-case fallback baked in too eagerly). Dropped the static; DHCP wins in every other environment (QEMU/SLIRP, GNOME Boxes, home LANs). `hpm refresh` now reaches `https://255.one/` cleanly. New regression `scripts/test_hpm_network.sh`. (`94f57ea`, `ea14914`, `0bdb550`) | **Done** |
| **ext4 multi-group alloc + 512 MiB files + live mkdir + cp -r** | A latent M16.61 limit (`ext4_alloc_block` only scanned group 0) caused sentinel writes to fail when group 0 filled. Extended both alloc and free to scan all groups (`3448ce0`). The long-standing M16.64 single-block write cap then fell — `ext4_write_open_file` streams across blocks, growing the inline extent leaf; files up to **512 MiB** (was 4 KiB). Bonus: O_TRUNC and unlink no longer leak blocks past block 0 (`a9b74dd`, `a7bd236`, `11d4b06`, `d2ed204`, `4f2def0`, `2abaf4b`). `vfs_mkdir` for `/ext/*` wires to `ext4_mkdir_live` (was EROFS); `ext4_open_create_or_trunc` rewritten subdir-aware so `cp -r` to `/ext/` lands fully (`b358cb1`, `674c248`, `69d08df`, `f42c9d3`, `85678dd`). | **Done** |
| **Installer: dd_blk → manifest-driven per-file install** | New `ext4_install_file_to_slot` primitive writes one file into an UN-mounted ext4 partition with save/restore of singleton mount globals (`a2b84c5`, `3df8013`, `b046cb6`, `1a1b97b`). Then `etc/install.hamsh` step 6 swapped from `dd_blk vdap4 → vdbp2` to `install_rootfs_from_manifest`, with the manifest generated by `scripts/gen_install_manifest.py`. New kernel helpers: `ext4_mkdir_at_slot`, `_ext4_walk_path_mkdir_p`, `ext4_blob_save_at_path`, `_ext4_dir_create_child` (`e643062`, `aecb48e`, `56335a2`, `5e61106`). ESP/FAT12 side still uses `dd_blk` (separate followup). | **Done** |
| **Component-package split — 17 packages + `hamnix-base` metapackage** | The monolithic `hamnix-base` (30-file blob) split into 15 logical components: `hamnix-kernel`, `hamnix-init`, `hamnix-hamsh`, `hamnix-coreutils`, `hamnix-net`, `hamnix-svc-sshd`, `hpm`, `hamnix-fs-ext4`, `hamnix-fs-fat`, `hamnix-drivers-{net-e1000e, block-ahci, block-nvme, usb-xhci, snd-hda}`, `hamnix-installer-tools` + `hamnix-bootloader` + `linux-debian-12` unchanged. `hamnix-base` is now a metapackage; hpm's existing BFS dep solver pulls every leaf via `depends:`. `TMPFS_MAX_FILES` bumped 256→1024 to fit the install closure. (`70ed290`) | **Done** |
| **Subdirectory channels at `255.one/` (Debian-shape)** | Per user 2026-05-27: *"non-free repo... I was thinking more of just a subdirectory; top level directories that each equate to a repository you can subscribe to."* Restructured `HamnixOS/packages` from flat to `/main/` + `/non-free/` + `/non-free-firmware/`. `hpm channels` / `enable` / `disable` subcommands; `/etc/hpm/channels` + `/var/lib/hpm/channels` (default: `main` only). Per-pkg `channel` field routes installs. Live: 17 packages at `https://255.one/main/index.json`; placeholders at the other two channels. (`fcc1641`, `cff568a`, `bf6179a`, `7f25aac`, `b06c8e7`; `HamnixOS/packages` commits `38f2c33` + `0a640ea`; build_packages.py `ensure_ascii=False` at `db00cb3`). | **Done** |
| **`man` + `help` discovery system** | ~20 markdown pages at `/usr/share/man/<topic>.<N>.md` (sections 1/4/5/8). `user/man.ad` opens + cats; `user/help.ad` walks the directory + extracts H1 summaries (`help` alone) or delegates to `man` (`help <topic>`). In-shell `help` builtin deleted in favour of `/bin/help` so it accepts args. (`8503b1e`, `1cf57b8`, `cb44aa5`, `0f3fbe8`, `5f1a7ff`, `eb73777`, `0d53243`, `0ca6a9f`) | **Done** |
| **Real-time `date` + `/proc/realtime`** | RTC driver (`drivers/rtc/cmos.ad`) already existed; added `/proc/realtime` procfs endpoint (`<ISO-8601> <epoch>\n<uptime.cs> <jiffies>\n`); rewrote `user/date.ad` from "uptime stand-in" to real UTC. Wall-clock = `rtc_boot_epoch + tsc_monotonic_ns()/1e9`. (`e5eb459`, `ebd8c24`, `10cc8f1`, `a54c03c`) | **Done** |
| **Persistent svc logs at `/var/log/svc/<name>.log`** | Each managed service's stdout+stderr captured for the lifetime of the boot, append semantics across `svc restart`. Plan-9-shape: new `DEVFD_FILE_APPEND` cdev kind + `OPENCHAN_APPEND` open mode + `tmpfs_open_for_append`. Child stdio binds via `/fd/1`+`/fd/2` namespace bind (NOT Linux dup2). (`2264e92`, `4f8b794`) | **Done** |
| **hamsh builtin redirects** | `echo "foo" > /tmp/x` silently dropped the redirect because builtins bypassed `_wire_redirects`. Fixed via in-process `sys_dup2` save/restore (no fork): 10 builtins now honour `>`/`>>`/`<`/`2>`/`2>&1`. Bonus latent fix: external `>>` was using `OPENCHAN_TRUNC` (silently truncating); now correctly routes through `OPENCHAN_APPEND` + `DEVFD_FILE_APPEND`. (`18d0f51`, `bdb23ec`, `c8d1b72`, `34457b6`, `abd9107`) | **Done** |
| **hamUI Phase 1 — AI-debuggable file tree per window** | Renamed `docs/rio.md` → `docs/hamUI.md` (Plan 9 name collision; design overlay H-§A through H-§F captured before implementation). Phase 1 ships `/dev/wsys/1/{text,output,cmd,ns,pid,uid,kind,geometry}` + `/dev/wsys` listing. Strategy: **kernel-side tee on `devcons_write`/`_read` into wsys rings + cmd queue** — ZERO hamsh refactor required. End-to-end cmd-injection round-trip works: an external `echo "ls /etc" > /dev/wsys/1/cmd` arrives at hamsh's readline indistinguishable from a keystroke. 12/12 assertions PASS. Multi-window-ready. (`cda060e`, `abae723`, `025c7b1`, `32bb867`, `8f833cd`, `425486a`, `df962fe`) | **Done** |

**Headline of this wave:** Hamnix crossed from "shippable distro
skeleton" to "useable Unix/TempleOS competitor + Plan-9-useable"
per user goal. ext4 went from 4 KiB-cap files to 512 MiB; the
installer dropped its dd_blk crutch; packages split into 17
components published via Debian-shape subdirectory channels at
`https://255.one/main/`; `date` prints real time; man/help solves
discoverability; `>` works on builtins; persistent svc logs hit
disk. And the strategic deliverable — **hamUI Phase 1, the AI-
collaboration unlock** — landed: an AI agent can `cat
/dev/wsys/1/text` to see what's on the user's screen and
`echo cmd > /dev/wsys/1/cmd` to drive it. Next-up (in flight at
the close of the wave): hamUI Phase 2 multi-window + `/dev/urandom`
+ NTP client.

## Wave — 2026-05-28: power management + parallel-track resumption

Trajectory reaffirmed with user (*"Ultimately I wanna do it all. We
can parallelize however possible."*): pursue every track — native
hamUI, the Linux X11 bridge, the CLI "survival primitives", and the
U-series Linux userspace ABI — choosing each agent by surface
disjointness rather than a fixed priority order. Agents run on
`claude-opus-4-8`.

| Item | What | Status |
|------|------|--------|
| **Real shutdown / reboot / halt / poweroff** | The three power binaries were print-only stubs. Now both a Plan-9-native `/dev/reboot` cdev (`DEV_REBOOT=26`) and the Linux `reboot(2)`=169 syscall funnel into one shared `arch/x86/kernel/power.ad::power_action()` core. It flushes filesystems first (`vfs_fsync_all` + per-block-device `blk_flush`), then: **poweroff** = ACPI-S5 ports `0x604`/`0xB004`/`0x4004` then `cli;hlt`; **reboot** = i8042 `0xFE` pulse with triple-fault fallback; **halt** = `cli;hlt`. `reboot(2)` validates the real Linux magics and is hostowner-gated. `user/{poweroff,halt,reboot}.ad` rewritten to write the verb to `/dev/reboot`. New regression `scripts/test_poweroff.sh` asserts the VM actually exits (not hangs) — both poweroff and reboot legs PASS. (`7ec38e8`, `2600da0`, `9e7c676`, `d28591b`) | **Done** |
| **Outgoing `curl` + `wget`** | `sshd` listened but nothing dialed out. The full HTTP/HTTPS-over-`/net` client buried in `hpm.ad` was extracted into a shared `user/http9.ad` (URL parse, IPv4-literal + `sys_resolve` DNS, tcp/tls connect via `net9`, GET with Content-Length drain, chunked-detect-and-fail). `hpm` refactored to consume it (no duplication). New `user/curl.ad` (body→stdout, `-i`/`-o`/`-L`) and `user/wget.ad` (body→file, `-O`). New `scripts/test_curl.sh` fetches HTTPS + HTTP from `255.one` and round-trips a wget save — PASS; `test_hpm_network.sh` still PASS after the refactor. ssh *client* deferred (separate protocol stack). (`87f1035`) | **Done** |
| **hamUI Phase 2 — multi-window + bg-shell routing** | `/dev/wsys/<N>/` is now wid-parameterised: `namec.ad` parses the window number out of the path and the wid rides the inline chan id's high bits down to the per-wid devwsys rings (no per-window cdev-slot explosion). `SYS_WSYS_ALLOC=293` / `SYS_WSYS_FREE=294` claim/release a wid for a detached child; `/bin/hamUI new\|list\|close` drives it. Background hamsh instances write to their own wid's ring and are gated out of the foreground serial console. The earlier "bg tee leak" turned out to be a **test serial-ordering artifact**, not a kernel bug — foreground detection was verified correct via kernel printk tracing; the fix widened the test's marker window. 7/7 phase-2 assertions PASS; phase-1 (13), poweroff, ntp, devurandom, installer_full, iso_qemu, e1000e_tx all still PASS. (`9e54879`) | **Done** |
| **Latent: `load_cr3+0x3` #DF (follow-up)** | A double-fault fires on the `ret` after `mov %rdi,%cr3` when a freshly-allocated CR3's kernel half is unmapped (stale/uninitialised PML4 entry; trap rsp is low memory). Pre-existing, surfaces in both ntpd/non-ntpd runs but **after** test success, so the suite passes. Recorded for a dedicated fix. | **Open** |
| **Native ↔ Debian root isolation** | The `sysroot/` (native) and `distro/` (Debian) roots — both subtrees of the one ext4 — are now genuinely isolated at the namespace layer, not just by convention. `etc/rc.boot.full` dropped its ambient `bind '#distro' /n/distros` leak (the distro tree is reachable ONLY inside the hermetic `enter linux`/`enter debian` namespaces); `etc/install.hamsh` re-binds it scoped to its own session. The deeper kernel fix is in `fs/vfs.ad`: a directory-open arm in `_open_named_subpath` (via `ext4_resolve_dir`/`_open_dir_ext`) so `ls /` inside `enter debian` works, plus write-side `_create_named_subpath`/`_open_hash_named_write` wired into `vfs_open_write`'s `#`-arm so distro writes (apt/dpkg) compose through the frozen `distro` prefix and can only land under `distro/`. New gate `scripts/test_img_distro_isolation.sh` boots `build/hamnix.img` under OVMF and asserts roots A/B/C/D/D' stay separate across a distro-side write — all PASS. (`7ac3e14`, `81e5316`) | **Done** |

## Wave — 2026-05-29..30: hamUI graphics + SMP + security hardening + compiler fixes

A high-tempo parallel-agent wave delivering the first graphical desktop
(hamUI Phases 4a–4c), real SMP with APs wired into the scheduler,
multi-user auth, syscall security hardening, virtual terminals, X11
prototype, and a batch of Adder compiler correctness fixes.

| Item | What | Status |
|------|------|--------|
| **Adder inlined in-tree** | `HamnixOS/adder` submodule replaced with a direct in-tree copy at `adder/`. The `compiler/` symlink and `LANGUAGE.md` symlink continue to point into `adder/`. `git clone` no longer requires `--recurse-submodules`; the `packages` submodule at `packages/` remains. (`9a8801e`) | **Done** |
| **Adder compiler: adjacent string concat, compound assignment, chained-compare fix, sizeof/min/max/abs/strlen/clamp builtins** | Several batch compiler improvements: `"a" "b"` concatenates adjacent string literals; `+=`/`-=`/`*=`/`&=`/`\|=`/`^=` compound-assignment operators; chained-compare (`a < b < c`) was miscompiled (each leg compared the original left operand, not the intermediate result); `sizeof`, `min`, `max`, `abs`, `strlen`, `clamp` added as compile-time builtins. (`ac389fd`, `02c8f1b`, `360bc0b`) | **Done** |
| **hamUI Phase 4a — layered draw protocol** | `/dev/wsys/<wid>/draw/<layer>/{kind,z,opacity,geometry,markup,fb}` + `ctl` verbs (`mklayer`/`rmlayer`/`setz`/`ls`) under `sys/src/9/port/devwsys.ad`. No rasterisation — just the file surface. (`b5ff553`) | **Done** |
| **hamUI Phase 4b — `hamUId` userland renderer** | `user/hamUId.ad` daemon: hamML parser, bitmap-font rasteriser, compositor, non-blocking `/dev/cons` integration. (`2e5ac90`, `af9ec01`) | **Done** |

GNOME2/MATE-style panel with Applications menu, window-list taskbar (buttons per open window, minimized shown dimmed), minimize-box, and live clock (HH:MM, updated per second from `/proc/realtime`). Interactive windowed hamsh terminal with VT-sequence emulation per window. (`7fe663b`, `f530ec0`, `d31a9ea`, `dc8a3c9`, `e9e2ef8`, `e1ba08d`, `89d699d`, `3db6e56`) | **Done** |

| **Multi-user auth — end-to-end** | `useradd` / `passwd` / `login` / `su` / `whoami` real implementations. `/dev/auth` gains `setpass` verb. New `SYS_SETUID_AUTH=300` syscall lets login/su atomically verify password and change uid without a window. `scripts/test_multiuser_auth.sh` covers all five binaries. (`57e0892`) | **Done** |
| **hamsh job control** | `&` background operator, `jobs` / `fg` / `bg` builtins, Ctrl-Z → `SIGTSTP` / `SIGCONT`. Process groups (`pgid == leader pid`) tracked in a 32-slot job table. (`ecbe9fd`) | **Done** |
| **Native runlevels + declarative services** | hamsh PID-1 supervisor gains `runlevel: N` bitmask field in service declarations (bit N = belongs to that runlevel). `service` + `initctl` CLI. Default multi-user runlevel 3; runlevel 0 = halt/poweroff, 6 = reboot. (`6fd5552`) | **Done** |
| **Virtual terminals VT1..VT4 + chvt** | `sys/src/9/port/devvt.ad` — four virtual terminals on `/dev/vt/1`..`/dev/vt/4` + `/dev/vt/ctl` for active-VT switching. `user/chvt.ad` writes the VT number to `/dev/vt/ctl`. Alt+F1..F4 keyboard shortcuts wired. (`80d8d0a`) | **Done** |
| **X11 first slice** | `user/x11/x11srv.ad` — a native Adder X11 core-protocol server listening on TCP port 6000 over `/net/tcp`. Handles `CreateWindow`, `MapWindow`, `PolyFillRectangle`, `CreateGC`, `PutImage`, and a sentinel `InternAtom` for clean shutdown. `user/x11/x11test.ad` demo client draws a coloured rectangle and verifies the server. (`05d050f`) | **Done** |
| **SMP: MADT-driven N-AP bringup** | `arch/x86/kernel/smp.ad` parses ACPI MADT Type-0 (Local APIC) entries via `drivers/acpi/acpi.ad`; boots each AP via INIT-SIPI-SIPI; sets up per-AP `%gs` + `LAPIC` + TSS; tracks all CPUs online via `cpus_online`. Falls back to APIC ID 1 when no MADT is present. (`a370b45`) | **Done** |
| **SMP: APs wired into scheduler** | `kernel/sched/core.ad` gains: test-and-set `rq_lock` spinlock (`spinlock_asm.S`); `current_idx` promoted to `Percpu[uint64]` so each CPU tracks its own current task independently; `sched_ap_idle_loop` idle kthread per AP — picks `STATE_READY` kernel tasks from the shared runqueue. APs are now full scheduler participants. Single shared runqueue (per-CPU runqueues / load balancing are follow-up). (`9a9c2b5`, `69c2bc4`) | **Done** |
| **Syscall-boundary access_ok hardening** | `arch/x86/kernel/syscall.ad` gains `access_ok(uptr, length)` and `access_ok_str(uptr)` validators that reject kernel-address (≥ 0x8000000000000000) userland pointer arguments. Wired to every native write/read syscall path that accepts a user pointer. Fuzz test: 200 kernel-address probes all return `-EFAULT`. (`e502c3d`) | **Done** |
| **Network packet parser hardening** | DHCP, DNS, TCP, ARP, HTTP parsers audited and hardened against malformed/oversize input: bounds checks on every field, length validation before dereferencing, truncation of oversized names/responses. (`11db3d9`) | **Done** |
| **TCP loopback smoke test** | In-kernel TCP loopback: `tcp_listen` + `tcp_accept` + `tcp_connect` + `tcp_send` + `tcp_recv` round-trip over `127.0.0.1`. Validated by the IP loopback shortcut (no NIC needed). (`0d2cb0d`) | **Done** |
| **Real TCP checksum + kernel_sendto/recvfrom** | TCP checksums computed over real pseudo-header. `kernel_sendto`/`kernel_recvfrom` (L-shim BSD socket ABI) wired to the in-kernel TCP stack. (`23dddb8`) | **Done** |
| **Per-class memory-leak accounting** | `mm/sched` gains a per-class accounting soak test that boots, allocates across slab/pages/VMA/task, then checks that freeing returns all counters to baseline. Guards against future allocation leaks. (`fddb384`) | **Done** |
| **CI: auto-publish hpm package channel** | GitHub Actions auto-publishes the `packages/` submodule to `https://255.one/` on every `main` push. Requires the `PACKAGES_DEPLOY_TOKEN` secret. (`92d8642`) | **Done** |

**Headline of this wave:** Hamnix now has a real graphical desktop —
hamUI Phases 4a+4b+4c all landed; `hamUId` renders markup to the
framebuffer with a classic GNOME2-style panel, taskbar, minimize, and
clock. The kernel runs on all available CPUs (MADT-driven AP bringup,
APs wired into the scheduler). Multi-user auth (`useradd`/`passwd`/
`login`/`su`/`whoami`) is end-to-end. Shell job control (`&`/`fg`/
`bg`/`jobs`/Ctrl-Z), virtual terminals (VT1..VT4 + chvt), a native vi
editor, tar/gzip, native cron daemon, and concurrent httpd are all
real. X11 core-protocol server prototype in `user/x11/`. Adder
inlined in-tree (no submodule). Syscall boundary hardening closes a
kernel-address EFAULT injection class.

---

## Wave — Kernel maturity, security & Linux-ABI depth (2026-06)

A long autonomous parallel-agent run (204 commits since the previous
wave) taking Hamnix from "boots a desktop" to a credible Linux/Unix
competitor: real process/memory/scheduler primitives, a security
baseline (W^X + NX + ASLR + seccomp), deep `/proc` fidelity, a real
uaccess layer, and broad driver/filesystem maturity.

### Process, memory & scheduling

| Item | What | Status |
|------|------|--------|
| **Copy-on-write `fork()`** | Eager-copy replaced with a real private per-process address space: per-task PML4 cloned from a pristine boot snapshot, 4 KiB COW fork of ELF/brk/stack/mmap VMAs + `MAP_SHARED`. (`#143`) | **Done** |
| **`mmap`/`munmap` + demand paging + file-backed mmap** | Anonymous + file-backed `mmap`, demand-paged on fault; `MAP_SHARED` writable file-backed writeback through the VFS. (`#142`,`#194`,`#199`) | **Done** |
| **futex (FUTEX_WAIT/WAKE)** | Userspace-threading primitive; glibc pthread workloads (8 MiB stacks) run. (`#144`) | **Done** |
| **poll/epoll** | I/O multiplexing across fd backends. (`#145`) | **Done** |
| **Priority/CFS-lite scheduling + SMP load balancing** | Per-CPU runqueues, nice/priority, user-task load balancing across APs. (`#151`,`#139`) | **Done** |
| **Memory pressure: swap + reclaim + OOM killer** | Page reclaim under pressure, swap, an OOM badness heuristic with `oom_score_adj` bias. (`#167`,`#236`) | **Done** |
| **MM Linux parity: rmap + active/inactive LRU + kswapd + writeback throttling** | Brings the memory subsystem to Linux `mm/` shape. New per-PFN struct-page array (`mm/page.ad`: flags/mapcount/LRU links/rmap word), carved from memblock after `cow_init` before the buddy allocator. **rmap** (`mm/rmap.ad`): per-physical-page anon reverse map (mapper slot+va) so reclaim/COW/migration locate a page's mapper without walking every task's page tables; single-mapper invariant for `MAP_PRIVATE` anon, COW-shared frames (mapcount>1) screened out. **Active/inactive LRU** (`mm/lru.ad`): intrusive lists threaded through the descriptors, second-chance/CLOCK promote-on-reference, `shrink_active` aging. **kswapd** (`mm/kswapd.ad`): low/min/high watermarks over (memblock headroom + buddy free), `kswapd_balance` background reclaim + `kswapd_direct_reclaim` under pressure. **Writeback throttling** (`mm/writeback.ad`): dirty/writeback page accounting wired into the `msync` MAP_SHARED flush + `balance_dirty_pages` over `dirty_ratio`/`background_ratio`. The LRU-tail scanner `reclaim_shrink_lru` (`mm/reclaim.ad`) evicts the coldest single-mapper anon pages via rmap; `reclaim_under_pressure` prefers it, falls back to the per-task RSS sweep. OOM killer kept as the last resort; demand-fault/swap-in record rmap+LRU+`mark_page_accessed`; `free_pages` unlinks LRU members + resets the descriptor. `scripts/test_mm_pressure.sh` PART C/D added (rmap, second-chance promote, rmap-targeted eviction + exact-byte swap-in round-trip, dirty accounting + `balance_dirty_pages` throttle). | **Done** — `test_mm_pressure` PASS (all PARTs A–D); `test_cow_fork` PASS (no COW regression). |
| **Kernel leak accounting + soak** | Per-class slab/page/VMA/task accounting returns to baseline after a spawn/reap soak. (`#128`) | **Done** |

### Security baseline (`#157`, `#160`, `#137`)

| Item | What | Status |
|------|------|--------|
| **seccomp-lite** | Per-task syscall filter (STRICT + lite allow-list bitmap) enforced at the Linux-ABI dispatch boundary; denial posts SIGSYS; inherited across fork/clone/execve. (`ccbca29`) | **Done** |
| **W^X — NX on data** | Stack/brk/anon-mmap mapped NX (PTE bit 63); exec-from-data → SIGSEGV. (`740c1c5`) | **Done** |
| **W^X — .text/.rodata read-only** | Non-writable PT_LOAD spans flipped RO after image install, before first user instruction; write-to-code → SIGSEGV; COW fork shares W^X pages verbatim. (`4cdff63`) | **Done** |
| **Stack-base ASLR** | Per-exec entropy-driven page-aligned user-stack slide (≤16 pages), wired into execve + SYS_SPAWN. (`600b141`) | **Done** — ET_DYN load-bias + interp + mmap-base ASLR followed once `#163` landed (`46491912`, see 2026-06-11 wave). |
| **Syscall-boundary audit + abuse test** | `access_ok`/`access_ok_str` reject kernel-address user pointers; fuzz coverage. (`#137`) | **Done** |

Gated boot self-test `fcache_selftest` (`/etc/fcache-test`, `scripts/test_fcache.sh`) proves page coherence, dcache namespace isolation + gen invalidation, icache hit/invalidate. Sits beneath the block buffer cache (`#395`), not replacing it. | **Done** |

(`#154`) | **Partial** — the SELF-HOSTED backend works and is now differentially fuzz-validated against the production backend (`scripts/fuzz_adder_diff.sh`: 100% accept + 100% correctness over 2400+ seeded programs on its supported subset, after fixing 5 sub-8-byte/signedness/immediate miscompiles). BUT the **default build is still driven by the Python backend** (`compiler/codegen_x86.py`, via `python3 -m compiler.adder`); `codegen.ad` does NOT yet drive any build path. **Headline of this wave:** Hamnix crossed from "graphical desktop on
SMP" to a real OS: COW fork, demand-paged mmap, futex, poll/epoll, full
POSIX signals, swap+OOM, and CFS-lite scheduling give it Unix process
semantics; a security baseline (W^X + NX + stack ASLR + seccomp + a real
`copy_to/from_user` uaccess layer) closes the obvious holes; ext4 gained
journaling + depth-2 extents + wstat; `/proc` reports real per-task
accounting; PTYs + interactive Linux-guest TTYs let real Debian binaries
run; and the driver surface (USB `.ko` metal path, audio, ACPI power,
TLS 1.3, ssh, Secure Boot) is broad. The open long poles are full
ET_DYN/mmap ASLR (gated on vaddr≠phys uaccess decoupling, `#163`), GPU
acceleration (`#182`/`#183`), aarch64 (`#175`), and the NUC USB metal
bring-up (`#238`/`#242`).

## Wave — 2026-06-05: namespace-purity base cleanup (Plan 9 file-server discipline)

| Item | What | Status |
|------|------|--------|
| **NVMe behind a PCIe root port** | `_nvme_pci_find_class` scanned bus 0 only, so the NUC's NVMe (behind a PCH root port on a secondary bus) was never discovered and the installer couldn't read the target disk. Replaced with a bridge-aware BFS scan (class 0x06/0x04 bridges enqueue their secondary bus from config 0x18; multifunction honored via header-type bit 7). `894baf8c`. | **Done** |
| **`/dev` + `/dev/blk` as bindable Plan 9 device servers** | `ls /dev` failed ("listdir failed") and `/dev/blk` was reachable only through a kernel literal-path string-match (`devblk_path_match`) — no directory walk, un-bindable, un-Plan-9. Introduced `#b` (block-device server → `/dev/blk`, lists registered devices via `blk_listdir`, `#b/<leaf>` → `devblk` backend) and reused `#c` as the `/dev` device-directory server (authentic Plan 9 cons-device model: serves `cons`/`null`/`zero` + the `blk` subtree). `etc/rc.boot` now `bind '#c' /dev` + `bind '#b' /dev/blk`; longest-prefix match routes `/dev/blk/*` to `#b` and `/dev/<other>` to `#c`. Stateful cdevs (`auth`/`fuse`/`ptmx`/`pts`/`loop`) rerouted through the `#c` leaf handler so `passwd`/`su`/PTYs/`losetup` keep working; console preserved via `#c/cons` → `FD_CONS_MARK`. `ls /`→dev, `ls /dev`→blk, `ls /dev/blk`→nvme0n1, `lsblk`, and `cat /dev/blk/nvme0n1/size` all verified green on `main`. `scripts/test_dev_namespace.sh`. `3a887b2c`. | **Done** |
| **`/net` as a bindable `#I` IP device server + drop the dead `/dev` literal arms** | The networking surface was reached only through `_open_net`, a literal `/net/...` string-match in `vfs_open`/`vfs_open_write` — the least-Plan-9 thing in the tree. Introduced `#I` (the Plan 9 IP letter; uppercase, no collision), `bind '#I' /net` in `etc/rc.boot`, and `devnet_listdir()` so the server is a real listable tree: `ls /net`→`tcp`/`udp`/`icmp`, `ls /net/tcp`→`clone` + live conn numbers, `ls /net/tcp/<N>`→`ctl`/`data`/`status`/`local`/`remote`. An open of `/net/tcp/clone` is rewritten to `#I/tcp/clone` by `chan_resolve_prefix` and served by the `#`-dispatch arm through the SAME `devnet` backend. DELETED the `_open_net` arms plus the now-dead literal `devblk_path_match`/`loopctl_path_match` interceptions (and the unused `devblk_path_match` import) — `/dev/blk/*` and `/dev/loop/ctl` are already served by the `#b`/`#c` binds. Verified green on `main`: `scripts/test_net_namespace.sh` (`ls /net`, `ls /net/tcp`, `cat /net/tcp/clone`) + `scripts/test_dev_namespace.sh` still PASS. `878e9a1b`. `/proc` literal bypass (`devproc_path_match`+`procfs_render`) is the remaining sub-task. | **Done** |
| **`/proc` as a listable `#p` device server — the LAST literal arm** | `/proc` already had a working `#p` open arm but bare `#p` returned ENOENT (no `ls /proc`) and two literal `/proc/...` interceptors (`devproc_path_match`, `is_proc_path`→`_open_proc`) still ran before namec in `vfs_open`/`vfs_open_write`. Added `devproc_listdir()` (bare `#p` → static well-known proc files + one decimal entry per live pid via the task-table walk `render_tasks` uses; `#p/<pid>` → the per-task leaves `status`/`stat`/`statm`/`io`/`limits`/`cmdline`/`maps`/`ctl`/`fd`/… validated by `task_lookup_by_pid`), wired into `vfs_listdir`'s `#`-arm exactly like `#I`/`#b`. DELETED the pre-namec literal arms so `/proc/...` resolves ONLY via the `bind '#p' /proc` → `#p/...` rewrite; kept the legitimate `devproc_path_match`/`_open_proc` fan-out *inside* the `#p` arm (reached only after the letter dispatch, not a bypass). `/sys` handling (`is_cgroup_path`/`is_node_path`, shared `proc_render`) left untouched. Verified green on `main`: `scripts/test_proc_namespace.sh` (`ls /proc`→cpuinfo + pid, `ls /proc/1`→status+stat, `cat /proc/cpuinfo`, `cat /proc/1/status`) + `test_dev`/`test_net` still PASS. `cc9443cc`. **Phase 2 COMPLETE — `vfs_open` now has ONE resolution path; zero literal special-cases.** | **Done** |
| **Real `mount()` — a VFS mount table replaces literal-path backend selection (Phase 3)** | Filesystems were SELECTED by ~70 hardcoded `is_*_path` predicate branches scattered across `vfs_open`/`open_write`/`listdir`/`stat`/`unlink`/`rmdir`/`mkdir`/`rename`/`symlink`/`link`/`truncate`/`chmod`/`set_mtime`/`resolve_backing` — the `/dev` literal-ladder disease applied to the whole storage layer, with no real `mount` at all (only namespace `bind`). New `fs/vfs_mount.ad` introduces a real VFS mount table: `vfs_mount(path, fs_kind, strip, shadow)`/`vfs_umount(slot)` (idempotent by mountpoint), longest-prefix `_mount_lookup_slot`, and three selection primitives the call sites now use — `vfs_fs_kind(path)` (→ backend id `FS_KIND_CPIO`/`TMPFS`/`FAT`/`EXT4`), `vfs_fs_rel(path)` (backend-relative tail with the mountpoint prefix stripped), and `vfs_fs_shadow(path)` (the `/var` tmpfs-first / cpio-baked-fallthrough rule). Base mounts register at init: `/`=cpio, `/tmp`=tmpfs, `/var`=tmpfs(shadow), `/mnt`=FAT (`fat_init`), `/ext`=ext4 (`ext4_init`). All ~70 dispatch sites converted to `vfs_fs_kind()`/`vfs_fs_rel()`/`vfs_fs_shadow()`; `vfs_open` gains ZERO `is_*_path` knowledge (worktree grep of backend-selection predicates = 0). Verified green: `test_dev`/`test_net`/`test_proc_namespace.sh` + installer Stage B (ext4 magic `0xEF53` written to NVMe through the new mount table). `a563d31b`. **Phase 3 COMPLETE.** | **Done** |
| **Unify fds on `Chan` — retire stateless cdev marks (Phase 4a)** | Fd TYPE was encoded in ~40 collision-prone `FD_*_MARK` magic-integer constants (history records real collisions: `FD_NET`==`FD_SIGNALFD`, `FD_AUTH`), each re-dispatched through a long `if file_idx == FD_X_MARK:` ladder in read/write/close/fstat — the fd-layer twin of the literal-path ladder. The correct abstraction (`namec.ad` `FD_CHAN_MARK` → inline-chan id `CHAN_INLINE_TAG \| dev_type` → one `_devtab_read`/`_devtab_write` switch on `DEV_*`) already existed but the migration had stalled. Retired the 13 STATELESS native synthetic-cdev marks (`FD_CONS`/`DEVNULL`/`DEVZERO`/`TIME`/`PID`/`RANDOM`/`MOUSE`/`CPUINFO`/`MEMINFO`/`UPTIME`/`LOADAVG`/`VERSION`/`HOSTNAME`): their opens now install `FD_CHAN_MARK` + `_chan_id_make_inline(DEV_<x>)`, behavior lives entirely in `_devtab_read`/`_devtab_write` (added `DEV_NULL`/`DEV_ZERO`), and the per-mark read/write/close/fstat arms + the 13 constants were deleted (net −142 lines). Console detection now resolves `DEV_CONS` via `namec_chan_dev_type` (also closed a latent bug where a namec-opened `/dev/cons` fell through to the cpio path with a bogus index). Stateful native fds (ext4/tmpfs/fat/buffer/dir/pipe/socket/blk/…) keep their marks pending a pool-`ChanT` lifecycle (Phase 4b); Layer-2 linux_abi event fds stay marks by design (boundary-discipline law). Verified green: `test_dev`/`test_net`/`test_proc_namespace.sh`. `091fde11`. **Phase 4a COMPLETE; 4b (stateful) deferred.** | **Done** |
| **Unify fds on `Chan` — stateful native fds via pool `ChanT` (Phase 4b)** | Stateful fds (per-fd cursor/inode/buffer state) couldn't ride the inline-chan-id encoding, so `FD_PROC`/`FD_AUTH`/`FD_BLK`/`FD_LOOP` still lived as magic marks. Introduced the pool-`ChanT` lifecycle in `sys/src/9/port/namec.ad`: a `chan_pool: Array[512, ChanT]` of real chan records (`in_use`/`dev_type`/`mode`/`srvfd`/`p9_fid`/`back_slot`/`refcount`/`back_ptr`), pool chan ids distinct from inline ids, fd shape = `FD_CHAN_MARK` + `fd_buf`=chan id + `fd_pos`=cursor, and ONE release path (`close_fd_in_task` → `namec_close` → per-`dev_type` release arm → `_chan_free`). Folded `/proc` per-pid leaves (`DEV_PROC`=63), `/dev/auth` (`DEV_AUTH`=64), `/dev/blk/*` (`DEV_BLK`=65), and `/dev/loop/ctl` (`DEV_LOOPCTL`=66, now a devtab cdev) onto pool chans; deleted their mark constants + dispatch arms, fixing two legacy auth bugs en route. NEW gates: `scripts/test_authdev.sh` (real `su` round-trip — `/dev/auth` written/read/consumed by `SYS_SETUID_AUTH` through the `DEV_AUTH` pool-chan path) and `scripts/test_loopctl.sh` (real `losetup` + `cat /dev/blk/loop0/size` = 32768). Verified on branch (heartbeat 26 ticks, `test_loop`, `test_devproc` 9/9, `test_fd_marker_uniqueness` 33 marks) AND post-merge on `main` (heartbeat 24 ticks / `test_authdev` / `test_ext4` all PASS). `40b16398`+`043a8962`, merge `5b3cea28`. Remaining stateful ranges → Phase 4c: `FD_DEVFD` (26 sites/5 files — needs a `DEV_DEVFD` arm in `namec_poll_readable` or `/fd/N` polls regress always-ready), `FD_PIPE_R/W` (48 sites/8 files), `FD_SOCKET`+`SOCKETPAIR` (89 sites/15 files). | **Done** |
| **#410 — installer image is a first-class LIVE image: real Debian dpkg runs in the live linux ns** | The TOP-PRIORITY ship-vehicle directive: `build/hamnix-installer.img` must be a Linux-live-style "try before install" with full native userland AND a live Debian namespace. `enter linux { /usr/bin/dpkg --version }` SIGSEGV'd with a W^X write-fault. THREE stacked kernel bugs root-caused in failure order: **(1) ext4 sparse-hole read truncation (primary)** — `_ext4_logical_to_physical()`=0 for a hole was treated as EOF by `ext4_read_file`, so mke2fs -d's sparse ld-linux-x86-64.so.2 (225672 B, extents with holes) read back truncated at 164864 B, losing .rodata/.got/.data → ld.so executed garbage and wrote into its own RO mapping. Fix (`fs/ext4.ad`): holes zero-fill and continue (Linux semantics) in `ext4_read_file`/`_ext4_verity_read`/`_ext4_fscrypt_read`. **(2) st_ino aliasing on recycled chan ids** — glibc dedups DSOs by (st_dev,st_ino); `vfs_fd_inode` keyed st_ino off the recycled pool-chan id, aliasing libselinux.so.1 to libmd.so.0 ("version LIBSELINUX_1.0 not found"). Fix (`fs/vfs.ad`): stable identity — ext4 on-disk inum (tag `0x41…`) / tmpfs slot (tag `0x42…`). **(3) vDSO tick-writer #PF at CPL0** — `vdso_update_time` wrote through the identity-low va, which is USER+RO+NX under a Linux task's PML4 and CR0.WP applies at ring 0. Fix (`linux_abi/vdso.ad`): vdso pages live in kernel-image .bss; kernel writes via the stable high-half kva. Plus two exec-path use-after-frees in `fs/elf.ad` (ns_blob single-entry cache kfrees the borrowed app blob during PT_INTERP recursion: RO-span snapshot before recursion; `elf_is_linux_binary` sniffed before load), and the live-debian gate now always rebuilds the image (no stale-image false greens). NEW gate `scripts/test_installer_live_debian.sh` FULLY GREEN on merged `main` ("Debian 'dpkg' ... version 1.22.22" banner); heartbeat (24 ticks) + ext4 (59 entries) + DE runlevel5 + thread_leader_exit all PASS. Branch `168857fb`+`f907e818`+`3d6b2fea`, merge `fb9e1b0d`. VM-verified. | **Done** |

**Architecture mandate opened (the base-shape track).** The `/dev` fix is the
reference template for a deeper cleanup: the kernel VFS currently resolves many
paths through a hardcoded literal-string ladder (`devblk_path_match`,
`loopctl_path_match`, `_open_net` for `/net`, `devproc_path_match`/`procfs_render`
for `/proc`) *before* — and mostly instead of — the real namespace machinery, and
the on-disk/synthetic filesystems are selected by ~53 `is_*_path` predicate
branches with **no real `mount()`** at all (only `bind`). Per user direction, the
endgame loop will eliminate **all** literal-path bypasses (everything becomes a
`#X` file server bound by init), then introduce a real `mount` so ext4/fat/tmpfs/cpio
attach at namespace points, then unify every fd onto the `Chan` abstraction
(retiring the ~24 collision-prone `FD_*_MARK` magic-integer ranges). Big-bang
rewrites are sanctioned where they're the right fix; each phase must still boot +
pass the test sweep.

## Wave — 2026-06-10: DE feature depth + userland TUI/CLI breadth

| Item | What | Status |
|------|------|--------|
| **Mouse scroll-wheel → focused-window scroll** | End-to-end wheel path: `drivers/usb/hid.ad` reads the boot-mouse byte-3 signed wheel delta only when the report `length >= 4` and threads it through a parallel `dz` side-channel (`mouse_rx_push_dz`) so the legacy packed-int32 mouse word stays byte-for-byte unchanged; `drivers/input/auxmouse.ad` `MouseEvent` gains a real `dz` field + `mouse_rx_pop_dz`; `sys/src/9/port/devmouse.ad` emits a 4-field `<dx> <dy> <btn> <dz>` packet (legacy 3-field parses as dz=0); `user/hamUId.ad` `daemon_apply_packet` parses the optional 4th field and (gated `dz != 0`) calls new `daemon_scroll_focused`, injecting Up/Down arrow CSI runs into the focused window's stdin. Pure-motion cursor fast-path untouched (verified backward-compat). `8cf14f51`. (`#416`) | **Done** |

## Wave — 2026-06-11: serial-console integrity + DE applet real backends

| Item | What | Status |
|------|------|--------|
| **Serial-console corruption fix** | Every spawned program wrote up to 5 garbage bytes (`66 90 66 90 5b` — linker NOP padding + a stray `[`) after its `[runtime:NAME] _start` banner: `user/runtime.S` computed the banner length as `$__runtime_start_mark_end - __runtime_start_mark`, which `as` folds to the WEAK fallback string's 25 bytes while the `leaq` relocation resolves to the strong per-binary string (e.g. 20 bytes for `wc`). The stray bytes also cleared `printk_at_line_start`, eating the next printk's `[00NNNN] ` prefix and defeating anchored test greps. Fix: the compiler-synthesized progname.o now emits a strong `__runtime_start_mark_len` data quad folded against its own labels; `_start` loads the length via the same weak-override relocation as the pointer. Plus a REAL serialization gap closed: `early_putc_user` hit the UART lock-free, so on `-smp 2` user bytes could interleave mid-printk-line — `console_tx_lock` moved into `early_8250.ad` (printk holds per message, `early_putc_user` per byte; trap/panic `early_puts` paths stay lock-free). (`03fe5d7e` via merge `4c8bf5c5`) | **Done** — VM-verified on main: `test_ext4.sh` full PASS (all 17 OK incl. 59-entry ls + FILE49), zero `\x90` bytes in the serial stream, heartbeat PASS. (`#437`) |
| **`test_ext4.sh` modernization** | Serial feeder gated on the hamsh readline marker + `FEEDER_SYNC` echo handshake instead of fixed sleeps (freshly-booted hamsh drops the first serial line); qemu timeout 55s→150s; root-dir count assertion updated 58→59 (the unconditional firstboot `.hamnix-grown` sentinel counts). The prior "FILE49 corrupted read" was three stacked artifacts: feeder input loss, the stale 58-count, and the banner-overrun garbage defeating the anchored grep — no ext4 read defect existed. (`98f9a1b7`,`ff6f23f2`) | **Done** (`#437`) |

Gate `scripts/test_u52_aslr_loadbias.sh`. (`46491912`) | **Done** — closes the `#157` security track (seccomp + W^X + stack ASLR + Stage 2 ASLR + uaccess audit all landed). |
| **`load_cr3+0x3` `#DF` root-caused: thread-group address-space lifetime** | The long-standing post-PASS double fault (TODO "latent crashes") was TWO defects — neither the suspected kernel-half-PML4 divergence (disproven; PML4s are memcpy-cloned from the pristine boot PML4, and a `[cr3-sync]` structural assert in `_free_task_user_pagetables` now guards the invariant). **(1) Reap-side (the latent `#DF`):** CLONE_VM/CLONE_THREAD and rfork-RFMEM threads share the creator's PML4, but `task_reap` unconditionally tore down the address space when the LEADER reaped while threads still ran — `vma_clear` freed the live worker stack, the brk arm freed live heap, and `free_page(cr3)` returned the live shared PML4 to the buddy allocator; once reallocated and scribbled, the worker's next dispatch did `load_cr3(garbage)` and the fetch of `load_cr3`'s own `ret` double-faulted — *after* PASS markers, so green tests hid it for months. Fix (`kernel/sched/core.ad`, `mm/vma.ad::vma_adopt`): exactly-once teardown by the LAST non-FREE referent of a shared mm, heir transfer of owner bookkeeping (image/interp/ustack phys, brk cursors, VMA list), thread-group zombie sweep. **(2) Creation-side SMP window:** `create_user_thread` published threads `STATE_READY` on a disposable boot-clone PML4 *before* the caller's `set_task_cr3` repoint — on `-smp 2` an AP steal could dispatch the stale clone. Fix (`sys/src/9/port/sysproc.ad`): new `share_cr3` param (no disposable clone, also kills a per-spawn page leak) + new `STATE_EMBRYO` state invisible to every dispatcher, flipped READY by `task_publish_thread_ready()` only after ALL inheritance stores. New gate `scripts/test_thread_leader_exit.sh` + static-PIE musl fixture `tests/u-binary/src/thread_leader_exit/` (uses raw `write(2)`: musl `exit()` permanently locks every stdio FILE and Hamnix `exit_group` doesn't kill sibling threads, so a survivor's `printf` deadlocks). (`557f6ee3`) | **Done** — VM-verified on main: tlx gate 3/3 PASS, heartbeat 24 ticks, ext4 full PASS. Side discovery: intermittent *pre-existing* ASLR reserved-bit-PTE fault on high load bias filed as `#438`. (`#76`) |
| **`#438` "ASLR RSVD fault" root-caused: `do_syscall` kstack overflow** | The intermittent reserved-bit `#PF` (user ifetch err=0x1d, coredump-read err=0x9) on high ET_DYN bias was NOT an ASLR defect — the draw only decided which physical pages sat below the kstack. Real cause: the Adder compiler gives every local a permanent frame slot (no liveness reuse), so `do_syscall`'s dispatcher accumulated a 28 KiB (0x6e10) frame under EVERY syscall; the Linux-ABI read/write bounce buffers (`u_read_body` 8.4 KiB, `_u_vfs_*_user` 4.1 KiB) stacked on top overflowed the 32 KiB kstack and scribbled kernel return addresses over the buddy block below — when that block was the task's own ELF-image page table (~1-in-4 ASLR draws), leaf PTEs became kernel-text pointers → RSVD `#PF`. Fix: out-line the KiB-buffer arms into `_sysarm_read/_read_nb/_write/_listdir` (frame now 0x2b90), heap-allocate `devwsys_text_read`'s 64 KiB scratch, bump `KSTACK_SIZE` to 64 KiB, stamp+check `KSTACK_CANARY` in `schedule()` (panics loudly on any future overflow). Validated by PINNING the ASLR draws to the exact captured failing biases (deterministic repro → PASS); pin knobs (`aslr_pin_*`, off by default) kept for future repro. New disassembly gate `scripts/test_do_syscall_frame.sh` fails any frame >0x3000. (`d91fb1c9`) | **Done** — VM-verified on merged tree: frame 0x2b90 PASS, tlx 4/4 PASS no `#DF`, heartbeat 26 ticks. (`#438`) |
