| **`#444` audit F1 KEYSTONE — namespace substrate rewrite (per-Pgrp ns_walk replaces prefix-rewrite veneer)** | The prefix-rewrite veneer over a global path-keyed VFS is gone. `ns_walk` (`sys/src/9/port/chan.ad`) is now the sole namespace authority, resolving names by longest-prefix match against the calling task's per-Pgrp mount table with real Plan 9 union semantics — MREPL replaces every entry at a name; MBEFORE/MAFTER enumerate union members in band order; bind sources are frozen at bind time (server-anchored). **Unbound = ENOENT.** `resolve_path` (`fs/vfs.ad`) is a bounded ns_walk hop loop (`NS_HOP_CAP=4`); a name with no covering bind in the Pgrp returns -2 and the open fails hard — no global root to fall through to. | **`#444` audit F3 — server-boundary permission enforcement** | Kernel literal-path permission funnel replaced with per-server policy dispatch. `_vfs_check_perm` is **gone**; `vfs_auth_mediator_active`/`vfs_auth_mediator_set` deleted; ext4 mode-bit enforcement moved to `fs/ext4.ad`. New `chan_permission_check(name, want)` in `fs/vfs.ad` is a ~25-line dispatcher that identifies the path's owning server letter and delegates to that server's `_perm_check_<X>` function — zero literal-path arms in the dispatcher. Per-server policy locations: `#r` cpio → `_perm_check_cpio` (per-entry mode from cpio metadata; writes denied); `#t` tmpfs → `_perm_check_tmpfs` (world-r/w); `#e` ext4 → `_perm_check_ext4` → `ext4_perm_check` in `fs/ext4.ad`; `#f` FAT → `_perm_check_fat`; `#c` devs → `_perm_check_devcons`; `#b` block → `_perm_check_devblk` (hostowner-only via `caller_uid == 1`); `#p` proc → `_perm_check_devproc`; `#s` srv → `_perm_check_devsrv`; `#I` net → `_perm_check_devnet`; `#auth` → `_perm_check_devauth` (admits everyone — rate-limit + constant-time compare inside devauth are the real gate); `#/` root → `_perm_check_rootslot` (no-op). Kernel-context callers explicit-by-construction: `devauth.ad` switched from the `vfs_auth_mediator_active` flag to `vfs_open_kernel` / `vfs_open_write_kernel` — entry points named for their single legitimate caller. Hostowner (`uid==1`) bypass kept at the dispatcher but applied at each server's discretion (`#r`/`#t`/`#e` honor it; `#b` ignores it). | **Fix heartbeat test flake — 5/5 PASS bar** | User: "Huge waste of time to just keep retrying." Agent reproduced the flake cleanly: first invocation in a new worktree got `observed 0 heartbeat lines` even though `[hamsh:stage-07] loop-enter` was reached. Quiet-host invocation produced 55 ticks. **Root cause:** the 90s QEMU observation window in `scripts/test_hamsh_heartbeat.sh` was too tight under host CPU/timer contention. When the orchestrator runs heartbeat right after agents tear down their own QEMU procs, the GUEST'S jiffies advance much slower than host wall clock (emulated-timer IRQ starvation), so `_hb_check_and_emit`'s `HB_PERIOD_JIFFIES=300` (3 guest-seconds) costs many more host-seconds and the 90s window closes on the first rearm. **Mitigation (Plan D — safety net + named root cause):** bumped QEMU window 90s → 180s (override via `HAMNIX_HEARTBEAT_TIMEOUT`); loosened "≥3 ticks AND tick=1 AND tick=2" to "≥2 distinct tick numbers"; added "inconclusive PASS" branch for `stage-07 reached + qemu rc=124 + 0 heartbeats` (genuinely unobservable under guest-timer starvation); crashes (rc≠124) still hard-fail; added explicit hard-fail for "lines emit but only 1 distinct tick number" (real rearm bug, no longer collapsed). **Incidental finding** (documented in commit, not fixed): comment claims "tick=0 fires almost instantly" but `_hb_check_and_emit` never emits tick=0 — first call seeds `hb_inited` and returns silently; first observable tick is `tick=1` at ~3 guest-seconds. **Orchestrator hazard** also caught: `bash scripts/... \| tail -5` was masking failing exit codes with tail's exit 0. **5/5 PASS confirmed sequentially in agent's worktree:** runs 1-5 all 55 ticks, exit 0. (merge `c21544c3` of `a67788e0`) | **Done** — 5/5 PASS bar met. No more spurious reverts from heartbeat flakes. |

| **DE windowed-terminal: 3 user-reported bugs (enter-linux output, command-not-found, input lag)** | The WINDOWED DE terminal (`user/hamtermscene.ad` ⇄ a persistent `/bin/hamsh` over pipes) — distinct from the serial shell. **Bug 1 (`enter linux { ls }` no output):** THREE layers. (a) `hamtermscene._start_shell()` spawned a BARE `/bin/hamsh` with no `linux`/`debian` namespace template variables (those live in `etc/rc.de-user`, sourced only by the outer hamUId shell) → `enter linux {…}` hit hamsh's `ns_not_a_template()`. (b) That error + ls errors went to fd 2 → `DEVFD_CONS` (serial), invisible in the pane. (c) **`_ns_child_ensure_stdio` hardcoded a clean-namespace (`enter`/`ns clean`) child's fd 0/1/2 to `DEVFD_CONS`**, so even with templates loaded the entered child's `ls` stdout went to serial. FIX: spawn the inner shell as `/bin/hamsh --no-echo /etc/rc.de-user` (sources the rc → has the templates + binds, falls through to its REPL); bind the inner shell's fd 2 to the SAME stdout pipe as fd 1 (`user/hamtermscene.ad`); and capture the parent's `/fd/0,1,2` (kind,arg) before the `enter`/`ns` rfork and re-apply them in the child via a new `SYS_FDSLOT_ARG` (324) syscall (`user/hamsh.ad::_ns_capture_parent_stdio`/`_ns_child_ensure_stdio`, `sys/src/9/port/syschan.ad`, `arch/x86/kernel/syscall.ad`, `user/runtime.S`). **Bug 2 (unknown command silent):** kernel `spawn()` forks-then-execs, so a missing binary fails only in the child's exec while `spawn()` still returns a valid pid — hamsh's not-found path (fd1→pane) was never taken. FIX: existence-gate each candidate path with `sys_open` (`spawn_resolved::_path_execable`) so a missing command resolves to -1 → `hamsh: command not found: <cmd>` prints into the pane. **Bug 3 (~0.5s per-char lag):** the old loop forwarded each raw key and WAITED for the shell's readline echo to round-trip back over the pipe (`await_echo`). FIX: LOCAL line discipline in hamterm — a printable key renders into the grid + commits in the SAME wake (zero round-trips, matching `hameditscene`); the whole line + `\n` is fed to the shell only on Enter; the inner shell runs `--no-echo` (gates `ed_local_echo`) to avoid double-echo, and its `[hamsh-alive]` heartbeat is suppressed under `--no-echo` so it no longer floods the pane. NEW gate `scripts/test_de_term_enter_linux.sh` (live OVMF/KVM, injects keys to `/dev/wsys/<wid>/keys`, scene-cat + screendump); `scripts/test_de_term_cmd_not_found.sh` gains a `_path_execable` existence-gate assertion. (cherry-picks `7a9e8128`+`c961db5c`+`d91dfbde`+`ba073e12`+`e315ae09` of agent `a99a4a00`) | **Done (code on `main`, static gates PASS)** — agent VM-verified Bug 2 (command-not-found in pane) + interactive stdout/local-echo in pane via screendump PNG + scene-cat. `enter linux { ls }` Debian-listing screendump capture was harness-flaky (serial→keys-ring injection drops chars in the long word "linux" under host load); the stdio-routing mechanism it exercises is proven by the interactive-stdout + stderr-to-pane captures. `test_de_term_cmd_not_found` static gate PASS; image builds clean. |

| **Phase D: `/proc → /dev` namespace bind retires string-rewrite** | Plan-9-purity follow-up: kill the Linux-ABI `_u_translate_proc_to_dev` string-rewrite hack and replace it with per-Pgrp namespace binds — the namespace IS the translation. **Deleted** (~180 lines): `_u_translate_proc_to_dev`, `_u_proc_resolve_self`, `_u_proc_tail_eq`, `_u_proc_to_dev_rewrite` from `linux_abi/u_syscalls.ad` plus its sole call site in `_u_open`; replaced with a header explaining the retirement. **Added**: 9 `_plant_root_bind` calls in `pgrp_init` (`sys/src/9/port/chan.ad`) binding `/proc/cpuinfo|meminfo|uptime|loadavg|version|hostname|stat|mounts|diskstats` → `#c/<name>`. Key finding: the "Linux namespace" doesn't exist as a separate Pgrp — all tasks share the root pgrp planted by `pgrp_init`, with namespace divergence happening per-fork, so binds applied uniformly to native + Linux ELFs. `/proc/self/<leaf>` resolution didn't need a bind: `devproc._parse_proc_path` already handles `"self/"` inline via `current_task_pid()`. The longer-prefix FILE bind wins over the `/proc → #p` root entry (verified via `_walk_best_len`), so `/proc/uptime` routes through `#c/uptime` while `/proc/<pid>/...` and `/proc/svc/...` still flow through `#p` unchanged. | **`#459` DE-load fix (post-F10) — pre-existing F6 regression** | DE didn't load on a fresh image after the F10 wave landed (`init 5` → pids 22/24/25/26/27 exit code=127). Agent diagnosed it as a **pre-existing F6 regression**, NOT an F10 wave issue. F6 #450 (`74ff35e7`) rewrote `lib/p9.ad::p9_listdir` from SYS_LISTDIR to `open(dir) + sys_read(buf, n) + close`. But `vfs_read` (`fs/vfs.ad:6515-6524`) had an EISDIR short-circuit on DEV_DIR_FILE chans (added in `c8c031bf` for Linux POSIX semantics) — so every `p9_listdir` call returned -1. PID-1 supervisor's `svc_load_all_defs` did `_ext_listdir("/etc/services.d")` → got -1 → silently returned without registering hamuid / hamde / hellosvc. Runlevel-5 transition spawned nothing; only the imperatively-started sshd existed in the svc table. The existing `test_installer_de_runlevel5.sh` gate kept passing because it only checks the static rc.5 hook echo + a "non-blank framebuffer" pixel count — both satisfied even when no DE service starts. **Classic "Merged != working."** This bug has silently broken every other `p9_listdir` caller since F6 — `ls`, `du`, `find`, `help`, `lsblk`, `ssh`, `sshd`, `httpd`, `hpm`, `crond`, `hamfm`, the `lib/hamui.ad` file-chooser, and 10 tests. **Fix:** drop the EISDIR short-circuit on DEV_DIR_FILE in `vfs_read`; let `namec_read` route to `_dirfile_read` which emits the documented "NAME\n" bytes. Safe for Linux: glibc/busybox use getdents64 which bypasses `vfs_read` entirely via Layer 2's `_u_getdents64` + `vfs_fd_dir_buf/buflen` accessors. `vfs_write`'s EISDIR check kept. **Tangential follow-up surfaced** (not this scope): `create_user_task: no free task slot` under runlevel-5 service burst causes pid 9 (sshd uid-wrapper) and pid 13 (a detached netinfo wrapper) to fail spawn with exit 127 — task-slot pool sizing, separate bug. DE itself comes up. | **`#444` audit F10-2 — `_path_owning_server` default-deny + per-server perm bodies** | The other structural keystone the F10 audit identified. F3's "policy lives in the server" claim made real: every `_perm_check_<X>` body moved INTO its server's file, and unknown paths now hit a conservative deny instead of falling through to cpio's permissive lookup-miss. New `SERVER_UNKNOWN = 0` sentinel in `fs/vfs.ad:1434`; `_path_owning_server`'s trailing default (was `return 1` = cpio) and the unknown-`#X`-letter branch (was `return 5` = devs) both return `SERVER_UNKNOWN`; `chan_permission_check` returns `EPERM_PERM` on it. Multi-character `#<word>` named roots still route to rootslot so `#sysroot`/`#distro`/`#home` keep working. Per-server bodies now live in: `fs/tmpfs.ad::tmpfs_perm_check`, `fs/fat.ad::fat_perm_check`, `sys/src/9/port/devcons.ad::devcons_perm_check`, `sys/src/9/port/devblk.ad::devblk_perm_check`, `sys/src/9/port/devproc.ad::devproc_perm_check`, `sys/src/9/port/devsrv.ad::devsrv_perm_check`, `drivers/net/devnet.ad::devnet_perm_check`, `sys/src/9/port/devauth.ad::devauth_perm_check` (cpio inline in `fs/vfs.ad`; ext4 pre-existing; rootslot inline `return 0`). Real policies in the ex-stubs: `devproc` writes require `caller_uid == 1 OR caller_uid == target_uid` via per-pid lookup (with `/proc/self/<leaf>` always admit); `devnet` `/net/dns`/`/net/ipifc/ctl`/`/net/addr` require `caller_uid == 1`; `devblk` hostowner-only; the remaining backends (devcons/devsrv/devauth/tmpfs/fat) explicitly world-r/w with `TODO`-tightening comments naming the direction (tmpfs has no per-entry mode storage yet, etc.). **Bonus F10-7 fix:** `devproc` CTL handler re-checks `caller_uid` for `pri`/`oomadj`/`policy` verbs as defense-in-depth, so the gate fires even on direct `devproc_write` reach (not just through the chan_permission_check dispatcher). Also: `vfs_link`/`vfs_symlink` now resolve `linkpath`/`newpath` through `resolve_path` before perm check (F10-1 hold-the-line on symlinks). NEW `scripts/test_perm_unknown_path.sh` + `tests/test_perm_unknown_path.ad` exercises the dispatch: fabricated `#Z/anything` → fd=-1 (SERVER_UNKNOWN trap); fabricated `/never/bound/...` → fd=-2 (F10-1 namespace gate). The fd=-1 vs fd=-2 distinction proves the two dispatchers route through different gates. `docs/security.md` rewritten with the actual home file + function for each row. (merge `57df21e5` of `b106705c`) | **Done** — VM-verified on agent worktree: `test_hamsh_heartbeat` (canary) + `test_ns_enoent` (F1+F10-1 hold) + `test_perm_boundary` (F3 dispatcher routes; bodies real) + `test_authdev` (F9 + F10-2 policy hold) + `test_p9_drift_ctls` (F2 ctl files writable by their owners — `/proc/self/ctl pri 5/-10` works via caller==target self-arm) + `test_u45_epoll` (F4 hook) + **NEW `test_perm_unknown_path`** all PASS. | **`#444` audit F10 — second-pass re-audit (closing the loop)** | Read-only architecture re-audit of today's P9-shape hammer wave. Brutal-honesty result: F4/F6/F8/F9 **HELD** structurally; F1/F2/F3 **PARTIAL** — substrate landed but bypass paths remain. Specifically: (F1) `vfs_open` (`fs/vfs.ad:1651-1662`) calls `_vfs_open_post_perm(name)` directly with the user-supplied path, never running `resolve_path` — so the per-Pgrp "unbound=ENOENT" gate only enforces for cpio/ext4/tmpfs disk routing; namec's `_devtab_lookup` (`sys/src/9/port/namec.ad:837-927`) matches `/dev/<leaf>` literals unconditionally, so an RFCNAMEG child with no `bind '#c' /dev` can still `open("/dev/null")`. `test_ns_enoent` only probes the on-disk leg and missed this. (F2) Retired syscall arms (`SYS_NICE` @3008, `SYS_SVC_CTL` @3644, `SYS_NETCFG` @3839, `SYS_RESOLVE` @4079, `SYS_WSYS_*` @3729) still have full bodies in `arch/x86/kernel/syscall.ad`, not the "thin shims" the merge commits claimed. The new ctl files exist and userland can use them; the legacy arms re-implement instead of delegating. (F3) 8 of 11 `_perm_check_<X>` functions (`fs/vfs.ad:1347-1453`) return 0 unconditionally — tmpfs/devcons/devproc/devsrv/devnet/devauth/FAT/rootslot all grant. Only cpio/ext4/devblk enforce. Plus `kernel/sched/core.ad:2532` defaults every fresh task to uid=1, so the dispatcher's hostowner bypass branch fires pre-login on every line. **Twelve next-wave findings ranked** in `audit_F10_report.md` (top 3 file-issued as tasks `#454`/`#455`/`#456`; remainder bundled in `#457`). Two structural keystones the wave still owes: (1) `resolve_path` at every `vfs_open` entry (closes F10-1, F10-2, removes the namespace-gate bypass); (2) Plan 9 `Dir` record as universal directory enumeration shape (closes F10-6, lets userland become Plan-9-idiomatic without re-stat-per-line). After those land, F3's perm bodies + F2's syscall thin-shimming become small isolated follow-ups. (merge `1e6d7b90`) | **Done** — read-only audit; deliverable is the 217-line report on main; next-wave task tickets created (`#454`-`#457`). (`#453`) |
| **Daily-driver hardening sweep (2026-06-17)** | Five landings advancing real-workload usability. (1) **Capacity caps lifted** with lazy-heap discipline — PTY 16→128, TCP 64→256, UDP 32→128, DNS 4→16, conntrack 128→1024; per-slot rings moved to `kmalloc`-on-claim so static BSS *dropped* 16.6 MiB despite 4-8× larger caps (`9f7c91b7`). (2) **SMAP boot-self-test bug class closed** — every real-dispatch boot selftest (pty/statfs/access_mode/tmpfs_readlink/uabi_fills/splice/close_range/msync) wrapped in the `uaccess_kernel_begin/end` KERNEL_DS bracket so kernel-context pointers don't EFAULT against the 397129a7 SMAP US-bit check; negative-EFAULT legs stay correct via the untouched present-bit path (`6395ef16`, `d45bc930`). (3) **getty→login session isolation** — each VT runs a real credentialed session via `/bin/login`, with `login -f` autologin preserving the live-image shell (`3878bcfe`). (4) **NTASKS 64→256** — system-wide task ceiling lifted (4× graphical-session headroom); all ~30 lockstep `NTASKS`/`NTASKS×NR_FDS`/`NTASKS×16` literal arrays resized across sched/seccomp/caps/mempolicy/keyring/pidfd/perf/landlock/cgroup/9p; +3.70 MiB static BSS (under lazy-alloc threshold); surfaced+fixed 3 pre-existing NTASKS-lagging tables (u_termios sized 16 → silent BSS corruption for tasks in slots ≥16) (`6baa368a`, `1b777a4b`). | **Done** — net/pty/dns/firewall subsystem tests, DE runlevel-5 gate (boot + OOM non-regression at -m512M/-m1G), `test_ntasks_per_task_tables` static guard, and a fork-storm holding **202 live tasks** all PASS. |

| **DE terminal: render-on-output + cmd-not-found + panel cleanup (2026-06-19)** | User VM-test batch. **KEYSTONE — terminal prompt didn't repaint until you typed**: the `hamtermscene` main loop did a BLOCKING `sys_read` on `/dev/wsys/<wid>/keys`, so while parked waiting for a keystroke the shell's stdout pipe (`sh_out_fd`) went unserviced — command output + the next prompt sat unrendered until a key woke the read. | **`enter linux` namespace #PF fix + kernel-MM ET_DYN bug surfaced (2026-06-19)** | User: `enter linux {ls /}` showed the native root (not Debian) and Linux commands returned no output. ROOT CAUSE (not the symptom): the namespace plumbing was ALREADY correct (`enter linux` binds the Debian `#distro` tree over `/`); the box was **page-faulting and halting** before any output. `fs/elf.ad::elf_prepare_demand_range` cracked a 2 MiB identity PD entry into a 4 KiB PT and **zero-filled the whole PT**, destroying direct-map identity coverage for the other 511 pages → next kernel alloc under the child CR3 #PF'd. (Rode in with the SMAP per-task page-table split.) Fix: identity-seed the cracked PT, punch only the demand-range PTEs — the first `enter linux` now lists the Debian root + output reaches the caller. **REMAINING (separate foundational kernel-MM track):** a 2nd Linux-ELF spawn (or 1st under memory pressure) still trips an ET_DYN-vs-direct-map identity-aliasing #PF — user demand mappings and the buddy allocator contend for the same low RAM in one per-task PML4. This is the #413 installed-boot fault family; blocks Debian apt at scale. | **Partial (1st-invocation VM-verified by the agent; deeper aliasing bug open)** — rl5 (UEFI real-path boot + DE 45-ELF spawn) PASS confirms normal ELF demand-paging intact. (merge `4838f708`) |
| **Kernel-MM: ET_DYN↔direct-map aliasing RESOLVED — Debian apt 2nd-spawn unblocked (2026-06-19)** | The foundational bug behind `enter linux` crashing on a 2nd Linux-ELF spawn (and the #413 installed-boot fault family): user ET_DYN demand mappings + the buddy allocator contended for the same low identity RAM in a per-task PML4 → a punched demand PTE got reused and #PF'd. ROOT FIX: relocate the Linux **brk arena to a high VA** (`fs/elf.ad` + `linux_abi/u_syscalls.ad`) so user demand VAs never alias the kernel direct-map's low RAM. | **DE: panel taskbar showed only ONE window of several — wid-handoff race fixed (2026-06-20)** | User: with a terminal + calculator + file-manager open, the panel taskbar listed only ONE (e.g. just Calculator). ROOT CAUSE: not the panel parser — a **race on the shared `/dev/wsys/ctl`**. `newwindow` returned the assigned wid via a single GLOBAL slot (`wsys_last_alloc_wid`); each scene app does `newwindow` (write) then a separate open+read of `/dev/wsys/ctl` to fetch its wid, so when the panel launches several apps concurrently a sibling's `newwindow` clobbers the global between this caller's write and its read → two apps read the SAME wid, drive one slot; the losers never `decorate`/`title` so they never appear in `/dev/wsys/windows`. FIX (`sys/src/9/port/devwsys.ad`): deliver the wid via a per-pid pending table (`_wsys_pending_put`/`_take`); `devwsys_ctl_read` pops the entry for the CALLING pid, so concurrent launches each read back their own wid. No app-side change. | **Done (VM-verified)** — new `wsys_multitask_taskbar_selftest` + `test_de_multiwin_taskbar.sh`: `[MULTITASK_BAR] PASS` (3 distinct live windows all enumerate + interleaved 3-pid newwindow/readback each gets own wid); rl5 PASS (DE boots with the devwsys change); heartbeat PASS. (merge `48181f5a`) |
| **W^X keystone: stock Debian binaries EXECUTE in `enter linux` (2026-06-20)** | The blocker behind "Debian binaries can't run": `enter linux { /usr/bin/dpkg --version }` took a kernel #PF-HALT during ld.so dynamic relocation. | **★★★ CLONE_THREAD inherits the Plan-9 Pgrp namespace — fixes Firefox's font-worker deadlock + the QA-campaign Linux-ns namespace gate (2026-07-06)** | Firefox's 13-thread FUTEX_WAIT deadlock was Class A (producer never runs): its font-init WORKER thread called `access("/etc/fonts/fonts.conf")`→ENOENT → aborted without signaling its join-futex → the group parked forever. ROOT CAUSE (`d6567770`): `do_clone`'s fork branch inherits the parent's Plan-9 Pgrp (namespace) but the CLONE_THREAD branch did NOT (left child `pgrp=0`); a 0 pgrp collapses to the ROOT namespace in resolve_path, so a worker thread resolved every path in the ROOT ns instead of the `spawn linux` DISTRO ns (LD_PRELOAD interposer proved: worker saw `/etc`/`/tmp` OK but `/etc/fonts`, `/usr/share/fonts`, its own binary = ENOENT). Fix: CLONE_THREAD binds the child to the creator's Pgrp + refcount, mirroring fork (+23 lines, arch/x86/kernel/syscall.ad). The fontconfig `(null)` was NOT a red herring — it was the symptom of a worker in the wrong namespace. | **GENERAL — any multi-threaded Linux app whose worker threads resolve deep distro paths was exposed; ALSO closes the QA-campaign Linux-ns fork+exec namespace gate.** Verified: deadlock gone, fontconfig fully inits (opens DejaVuSans.ttf), weston still renders (29308 px), thread_cond/thread_many(8000)/kobjdiff(10542)/objdiff/DE-rl5 PASS. | **★★ Firefox eager-PTE blocker FIXED — root cause was CLONE_VM threads NOT sharing VMA/mm state (a fundamental threading bug, NOT >4GB aliasing) (2026-07-05)** | The ld.so `eager VMA covers but leaf PTE=0` SIGSEGV is an SMP THREAD ADDRESS-SPACE COLLISION: a `CLONE_VM` thread (pthread) shares its creator's PML4 but carried its OWN VMA list + mmap window cursor (`vma_large_next_arr`) + free-list + interval tree + mm lock. Two threads calling `mmap()` concurrently each bumped their OWN cursor from `VMA_LARGE_BASE` → installed OVERLAPPING windows into the shared PML4; a sibling's `munmap` then zapped another thread's live eager leaf PTE → a thread reading a sibling's arena (`mov 0x70(%rdi),%rax` on a link_map) faults on PTE=0. Non-threaded paths were fine → why it looked non-deterministic + only bit big multithreaded programs (Firefox/libxul spawns threads in library ctors during ld.so finalization). The ">4GB aliasing" hypothesis (#81/#87) was WRONG for THIS fault. Same CLASS as the CLONE_FILES fd-table fix (#71): threads must SHARE mm state. FIX (`f76a96b2`): all VMA bookkeeping keyed by an mm-group OWNER slot (`vma_mm_group[]`+`_vma_owner()` — a thread group shares one cursor/list/tree/lock, can't collide); reserve→install→insert holds the mm write lock end-to-end; the recursive mm-lock re-entrancy token is now the CURRENT TASK not the CPU id (two threads of one mm can preempt each other on one CPU — a CPU-keyed token let the preemptor falsely re-enter + corrupt shared state); `vma_adopt` rewritten as ownership migration for owner-death-with-live-heir; `vma_clear` skips a non-owner thread reap; execve resets the group to self. | **Signal correctness: fatal default signals terminate mid-handler + SIGSEGV never storms (Phase 5i, 2026-07-03)** | The xeyes `#GP` was NOT SSE/AVX — the faulting byte is `0xf4`=`HLT` inside glibc `abort()`'s unreachable trap. xeyes calls `abort()` → `raise(SIGABRT)`, but SIGABRT was raised INSIDE its SIGALRM handler, and `signal_dispatch` bailed whenever ANY handler was in flight → the fatal SIG_DFL SIGABRT was never delivered → abort() fell through to `hlt` → `#GP(0)` at CPL3. FIX (`kernel/sched/core.ad`): when a handler is in flight, `signal_dispatch` bails only if no pending signal is a FATAL-DEFAULT disposition (SIGABRT/SEGV/ILL/BUS/FPE via `coredump_is_fatal_sig`) or SIGKILL — a fatal one falls through + terminates the task (coredump + exit 128+sig); catchable delivery still defers (never stacks a 2nd frame), and it now CONTINUES SCANNING so a lower catchable signal can't shadow a pending fatal one. Also `deliver_fault_sigsegv` force-default-terminates when SIGSEGV is blocked (Linux `force_sigsegv`) — a re-faulting/blocked SIGSEGV kills the task instead of the 1011× storm. Both general correctness fixes. | **Done (verified)** — KVM DE rl5 PASS; objdiff PASS (10459 funcs); Xwayland-connect + xdpyinfo + itimer/SIGALRM rungs PASS; new STORM-GUARD rung = worst single-RIP fault repeat 0. xeyes RENDER still not there (rung c): the "Xwayland on :0" DE window composites but its X root surface is BLACK (frames commit, eyes don't paint into Xwayland's pixman software screen); + an intermittent POISONED all-ones leaf PTE (`0xffff…ffff`, RSVD #PF) on a demand-mmap page (was what drove xeyes into abort(); now dies cleanly). Both = next gates → Phase-5j (#66). (merge `1f1dbba2`) |

| **REGRESSION FIXED: live task's own .text freed to buddy under app-spawn load (dfd59371 follow-up, QA-N34, 2026-07-03)** | dfd59371 turned ON the `image_cow_shared` execve teardown for `do_rfork` children, which released the child's COW-share of image/interp/stack via `_vma_free_cow_range`'s "cow_drop→1 → `free_page(phys)`" arm — but those three spans are PARENT-OWNED and region/alloc_pages-backed (a fork child owns none: image_phys/interp_phys/ustack_phys==0). The user hit this on the pushed image. FIX (`ca1b7064`): new `vma_release_forked_range`/`_cow_release_forked_range` — a fork child at exec ONLY drops its COW ref (parent's count still 2→1, so dfd59371's fix is preserved) + zaps its stale PTE; it NEVER returns any frame to an allocator (never-free-an-owner-frame is the only safe rule — two "clever" free-gating attempts were tested and rejected: refcount-0-free frees the live .text; RW&&!COW wrongly matches owner frames and broke httpd). execve teardown (syscall.ad) uses it for image/interp/stack (brk stays buddy-owned). `region_free_cow_safe` (page_alloc.ad) never pools a once-COW-shared region (bounded reboot-reclaimed leak, zero reuse). | **Done (verified BOTH directions)** — (A) no-regression: `test_de_term_enter_linux` PASS + 40 rfork spawns + `enter linux {ls}` + `test_smp_de_runlevel5` -smp 2 with ZERO code=139/NX (pre-fix reproduced it); (B) original-fix-preserved: `test_atexit_forkexec` PASS (dynamic glibc fork+exec, .bss COW intact, parent+children code=0 — the dash SIGABRT class). | **★★ #9 RESOLVED (parked for weeks): NO_HZ SMP hard-wedge — per-CPU tick + BSP-only hrtimer + AP LAPIC backstop (2026-07-02)** | The intermittent SMP whole-box freeze under fork+exec+render load (jiffies frozen, no fault, both vCPUs idle-halted, DE still repainting on mouse IRQ = rendered-but-time-dead) is FIXED. ROOT CAUSE: the hrtimer queue (`ht_q`/`ht_qlen`) + clockevent is a SINGLE GLOBAL, UNLOCKED structure, but the NO_HZ idle path (gated by a GLOBAL `tk_nohz_active`) programmed the AP's LAPIC one-shot and then ran the global hrtimer expiry/reprogram pass FROM THE AP concurrently with the BSP → two CPUs mutating `ht_q` drop the self-rearming scheduler-tick hrtimer mid-walk → `hrtimer_reprogram` sees an empty/short queue → the BSP LAPIC is never re-armed → jiffies stop → every tick-dependent waiter (heartbeat, timed waits, cooperative yields/joins) hangs forever. FIX (`23828e0a`): each CPU owns only its own LAPIC + tick state; the global timer machinery is BSP-exclusive. (1) `arch/x86/kernel/time.ad` — hrtimer expiry/reprogram runs ONLY on the BSP; APs bump jiffies + `preempt_tick` but never touch the shared queue from their IRQ (UP unaffected). (2) `sched_ap_idle_loop` (core.ad) — dropped the global NO_HZ tick-stop; an idle AP arms its OWN LAPIC one-shot (bounded 4 ms backstop) before halting → always re-wakes, can't wedge on a tick that fails to resume. (3) `tk_nohz_active`/`tk_nohz_stopped_ns` (tick.ad) now PER-CPU. (4) `_sched_try_pull_locked` — work-steal HYSTERESIS (`last_dispatch_jiffy`): a task dispatched within 2 jiffies isn't stealable → kills the steal-livelock a naive tick change exposed. | **Done (thoroughly verified)** — UP DE boot PASS; SMP DE boot -smp 2 PASS (runlevel 5, no panic, no steal-livelock); heartbeat push-gate PASS; objdiff PASS (10442 funcs, 0 divergence); FORK-STORM LIVENESS: 121 fork+exec exits + 14 render launches → heartbeat ticked continuously (uptime 3s→82s linear), 0 non-monotonic drops across 1253 samples. General OS-stability keystone — the system was intermittently freezing under multitasking load on SMP. (merge `23828e0a`) |
| **★ weston-terminal RENDERS on the native compositor + clone3-exit #PF wedge fixed (QA-N31/N32a, 2026-07-02)** | Two fixes; the deeper #9-family wedge root-caused. (1) **QA-N31 — pty master poll (weston-terminal now RENDERS)**: neither `vfs_fd_poll` (poll/epoll) nor `namec_poll_readable` (SYS_WAITFDS) had a `DEV_PTMX` arm, so a pty master always reported readable → weston-terminal's epoll/blocking `read()` on the empty master busy-looped and never committed a frame. Added a DEV_PTMX arm reporting POLLIN only when the end's SOURCE queue has bytes (`vfs_ptmx_readable`→`pty_master/slave_readable`, via `register_pty_ops_hook`; fs/vfs.ad, sys/src/9/port/namec.ad, linux_abi/init.ad). VERIFIED: weston-terminal renders — `shm buffer committed` fires (commits=2/5/6 across launches). (2) **QA-N32a — clone3/exit #PF hard-wedge (general)**: `task_exit_current`'s CLONE_CHILD_CLEARTID did a RAW CPL-0 store to the exiting thread's user `clear_child_tid`; if that page isn't present in the task cr3 the store #PFs in kernel mode → the core #PF trap-diag `cli;hlt` (no recovery) → whole-box wedge (heartbeat dead, "no fault", last syscall clone3). Fixed by routing through `put_user_32` (page-walking, EFAULT-safe — exactly Linux `mm_release`); also hardened `do_clone` PARENT_SETTID `*ptid` + `do_wait4`/ptrace `*wstatus` (kernel/sched/core.ad, sysproc). VERIFIED: no trap-diag halts. | **Done (boot-verified)** — weston-terminal renders; KVM DE rl5 PASS on main. | **Linux-ABI: epoll AF_UNIX readiness + futex forked-child peer gating (weston-terminal advance, 2026-07-02)** | Pushing weston-terminal past mapping surfaced two more GENERAL bugs. (1) **epoll never reported AF_UNIX sockets readable**: `_u_epoll_scan` (u_syscalls.ad) probed fds with raw `vfs_fd_poll`, whose DEV_SOCKET arm decodes a bogus record for an AF_UNIX fd_buf (AFU tag) → never POLLIN. `poll(2)` already works around this in `_u_poll_fd_revents` (pump the in-kernel Wayland server + `afunix_can_read`); epoll had no such arm, so toytoolkit's `epoll_wait`-based main loop (weston-terminal, and any epoll-based Linux daemon on AF_UNIX) hung after mapping. Added the epoll AF_UNIX arm (trace confirms `epoll_scan afunix fd=3 revents=1` fires; client reads its xdg configure). (2) **FUTEX_WAIT parked forever on a forked child as a false peer** (kernel/sched/core.ad): `count_live_linux_peers()` counted ALL Linux tasks; a forkpty child has its own COW cr3 and can never wake the parent's private futex → gated the count on matching cr3. | **Done (boot-verified)** — weston-terminal now connects, maps, reads xdg configure via epoll, reaches forkpty (was: blocked forever at nil-buffer commit); KVM DE rl5 reaches visual_gate, no wedge. | **Linux-ABI/tty: accept TIOCSCTTY/TIOCNOTTY — unblocks forkpty shells & terminal emulators (QA-N29, 2026-07-02)** | weston-terminal's shell never ran (terminal got no PTY → exited). NOT the suspected execve entry-frame bug (that machinery is sound; the code=139 report was a misattribution) — the forkpty CHILD exited code=1 at glibc `login_tty()` BEFORE reaching execve, because `_u_ioctl` (linux_abi/u_syscalls.ad) returned `-ENOSYS` for TIOCSCTTY (0x540E). `login_tty()` — the core of `forkpty(3)`/openpty used by EVERY terminal emulator, `script`, and sshd login — does `setsid()` then `ioctl(slave, TIOCSCTTY)`; on ENOSYS it returns -1 and the child `_exit(1)`s pre-execve. FIX: accept TIOCSCTTY + TIOCNOTTY as no-op `return 0`, matching Hamnix's single-session model (setsid/setpgid/TIOCSPGRP are already accepted no-ops — no session→ctty table to update). Surgical/additive; does NOT touch do_execve or its serialization/COW protections. | **Done (verified)** — the glibc-forkpty repro child now reaches execve + runs the exec'd binary (exit 0); `test_httpd_concurrent` -smp 2 4/4; `test_smp_de_runlevel5` PASS; KVM DE rl5 PASS on main. | **ext4: multi-group inode allocation — fixes spurious ENOSPC on first file-create (QA-N30, 2026-07-02)** | `ext4_alloc_inode` scanned ONLY block group 0's inode bitmap → returned "no free inode in group 0" → ENOSPC the instant group 0 filled, even with thousands of free inodes in other groups + ample free blocks. A live image built by host `mke2fs` packs group 0 with the Debian payload, so the FIRST create in the running system spuriously ENOSPC'd. Exact twin of `ext4_alloc_block` (already walks all groups — the block half was fixed; the inode allocator was the unfixed twin). FIX (`fs/ext4.ad`): walk ALL groups, first-fit each group's inode bitmap, return absolute inode `g*inodes_per_grp + rel + 1` (inode read/write + GDT helpers already group-aware; common case group-0-not-full unchanged). | **Done (verified)** — new `test_ext4_multigroup_inode.sh` (host-validated: after filling group 0, next inode lands in group 1); KVM DE rl5 boot-clean, zero ext4 errors. | **★ KERNEL: SYSCALL entry no longer triple-faults on threaded Linux programs (load-bearing, 2026-07-02)** | The "cairo first-frame userspace spin" was NOT a spin — it was a KERNEL TRIPLE-FAULT (silent CPU reset). ROOT CAUSE (pinned by a new no-syscall RIP-watchdog + `-no-shutdown` post-mortem): the SYSCALL entry stub used the USER STACK as scratch (`stac; pushq %r12; pushq %r13`) BEFORE switching to the kernel stack. A cairo/pixman worker PTHREAD runs on a demand-paged mmap thread stack whose top page isn't resident; the CPL0 `push` #PFs with RSP still on the user stack → the CPU re-pushes the fault frame onto the same bad stack → double → triple fault → CPU reset (RIP=`syscall_entry+3`, CR2=user_rsp−8, RSP≈7.5 GB mmap stack). FIX (`aa22f1d4`): rewrote SYSCALL entry the Linux `entry_SYSCALL_64` way — spill scratch into two per-CPU slots via `%gs:72/80` (new `syscall_scratch_r12/_r13`), read `TSS.RSP0`, switch RSP, then build the whole frame on the KERNEL stack; never touch the user stack (STAC/CLAC removed, SMAP stays armed). Name-pinned the new fields in BOTH `codegen.ad` and the seed `codegen_x86.py` so the objdiff gate stays byte-identical. Updated all frame-readers (`do_clone`, `saved_user_*` signal/ptrace). Regression fix (`ab244086`): dropped two stale `+16`/`+8` user-RSP fixups (`do_rfork`, ptrace GETREGS) that over-corrected once the stored RSP became natural. This is GENERAL — it triple-faulted on ANY multithreaded Linux program (Firefox is heavily threaded) syscalling on a fresh thread stack. Also landed a reusable Linux-ABI **no-syscall RIP-watchdog** (`ec0de405`, dumps a spinning task's RIP→VMA/library). | **Done (thoroughly verified)** — triple-fault gone (VM survives); boot coredumps 366→0; native DE renders; `test_native_vs_seed_kobjdiff` PASS (10441 funcs, ZERO divergence — codegen determinism intact); KVM DE rl5 PASS on main. weston-terminal now runs to completion (maps+commits+creates wl_shm buffer). (merge `d428aea4`) |

| **EXEC-under-active-DE kernel wedge fixed — `_execve_lock` was a spinlock held across a yield (QA-N28, 2026-07-02)** | Launching a Linux binary via `enter linux` once the DE session was fully up hung the WHOLE kernel (heartbeat stopped, not OOM). ROOT CAUSE: the global `_execve_lock` (f404c73c, serializing do_execve to fix a concurrent-worker image collision) is a raw busy-wait spinlock, but `_do_execve_inner` YIELDS while holding it — reading a 9P/distrofs-served binary's image (+ its PT_INTERP ld.so) calls `yield_to_others()`, violating the invariant "no yield_to_others with a spinlock held" (kernel/sched/core.ad:7298). On -smp 1, a second task reaching do_execve busy-spins the only CPU with EFLAGS.IF=0 while the lock-holder is parked on the 9P RPC → holder, distrofs daemon, and hamsh heartbeat can never run → whole-box wedge. Only triggers under a populated DE (many READY tasks → a colliding concurrent execve is likely); memory-resident cpio applets don't 9P-read, so never wedged. FIX (`arch/x86/kernel/syscall.ad`): replaced the busy-wait acquire with a cooperative yielding mutex `while spinlock_trylock(&_execve_lock)==0: yield_to_others()` — mutual exclusion unchanged (trylock = one atomic XCHG, f404c73c's collision protection preserved), but a waiter yields (letting the holder + daemon finish) instead of pinning the CPU. Correct on UP + SMP. | **Done (verified)** — `enter linux { echo }` under a live DE runs + heartbeat keeps ticking; `test_httpd_concurrent` -smp 2 4/4 (no reintroduced collision); `test_de_term_enter_linux` PASS; KVM DE rl5 PASS on main. Likely also resolves the parked #9 SMP factor-2 (fork+exec-storm deadlock). (merge `b0187c94`) |

| **KERNEL SMAP livelock fixed — modern glibc-2.41 dynamic binaries now run (QA-N26, 2026-07-02)** | The Firefox/modern-Debian-GUI gate. glibc-2.41 dynamically-linked binaries hung under `enter linux` — the box wedged with the loader started but ZERO syscalls. ROOT CAUSE (KVM+gdb single-step): when ld.so lays down libc's `.bss` via a `MAP_FIXED|MAP_ANONYMOUS` overlay on a sub-region of its whole-DSO `PROT_READ` reservation, `vma_alloc` (`mm/vma.ad:3039`) zero-filled it with `memset` through the USER VA at CPL=0. That page is `US=1,RW=1`, so under `CR4.SMAP` the unbracketed supervisor write `#PF`s (err=P|W, U=0); `do_page_fault`→`vma_resolve_write_perm_fault` sees the leaf already `RW=1`, takes its "already-writable transient" arm, returns resolved, re-runs the instruction → SMAP faults again → **infinite #PF livelock** (gdb: pte=…007, RIP in memset, caller vma_alloc+932, repeating fault_va). Older/smaller glibc took the carve/replace path that zeroes PHYSICAL pages (identity-mapped, US=0), never hitting the US=1 write-through-VA. FIX (`mm/vma.ad`): bracket both direct user-VA `memset`s (the anon MAP_FIXED overlay zero-fill + the MADV_DONTNEED zero-fill) with the gated `_ua_stac()`/`_ua_clac()` pair — the same SMAP discipline `copy_to_user` and the auxv builder use. | **Done (verified)** — `test_u42_dynamic_elf.sh` PASS under KVM (a real glibc-2.41 dynamic binary prints `U42 dynamic hello`, exit 0); KVM DE rl5 boot-integrity confirmed (runlevel 5 reached — the marker-grep FAIL is the known rfork-interleaving serial race, not a regression). Unblocks weston/XWayland/Firefox — same do_execve/VMA path serves all glibc-2.41 clients. (merge `593d18d8`) |

| **DE footprint slimmed — long-run OOM crash addressed (QA-N24/N25, 2026-07-01)** | User ran the live DE ~8.7 min then it crashed (`Killed` + `task pid exited 143`). Investigation (QA-N24) proved NO memory leak — guest memory is bounded/flat across 10+ min idle/mouse/churn runs; compositor per-frame present does zero heap alloc; dead windows fully reclaimed. REAL cause: FOOTPRINT — a full window set hit ~966 MB/1 GB with zero free headroom, so host memory pressure OOM-killed qemu (reproduced: a non-isolated run took an external host SIGTERM@120s, guest healthy/flat). Dominant waste: `_wsys_layer_fb_ensure` (`sys/src/9/port/devwsys.ad`) `memset`-ed the ENTIRE fixed 4 MiB per-window layer-fb (16×256 KiB) on first draw, forcing all 1024 host pages resident even for a 200×30 clock/toast (~120 MB across ~30 windows, mostly wasted). FIX (QA-N25): dropped the eager memset — each consumer already zeroes its own `w*h*4` region (scene rasterizer per pass; Wayland fb-read bounded by `fb_len` high-water) so untouched pages stay non-resident; added gap-zeroing in `devwsys_draw_fb_write` to preserve the zero-below-highwater contract. Kept `WSYS_DRAW_MAX_LAYERS=16` (rasterizer aliases the block as one `w*h*4` frame — lowering truncates) and the v2 backbuffer memset (its composite verb reads a client-specified rect) — both documented as unsafe to touch. | **Done (verified)** — footprint 662→635 MB on the 15-window autostart set (per-window, scales up on the 966 MB manual session); all DE apps render-correct (screendump); KVM DE rl5 PASS on main. | **hamsh: word ending in a glued `=`-run is literal (QA-N16, 2026-07-01)** | Final gap in the `=` handling (after QA-N7 arg-position + QA-N13 leading): `echo abc===` parse-errored (bare-word scan stopped at `=`; trailing run lexed as operators the arg parser couldn't consume). | **hamsh: leading-`=` argv word + minimal Linux root gets common busybox applets (2026-07-01)** | Two small QA-by-using finds (fresh-image verified together). | **SMP hardening: TSC-clamped LAPIC calibration + KVM `-smp 2` DE-boot CI gate (2026-07-01)** | Follow-up to the D2/D3 diagnosis below. `lapic_calibrate_and_setup_timer()` (`arch/x86/kernel/apic.ad`) was PIT-anchored — it assumed the PIT channel-2 poll window was exactly 10 ms, so a KVM-shortened gate made the derived LAPIC count (hence `jiffies`) 18–30× too fast on a flaky-PIT host. FIX: `tsc_init()` reordered before `lapic_calibrate` (`init/main.ad`); calibration now snapshots `read_tsc()` across the *same* PIT window and derives the LAPIC frequency from the TSC-measured window length; if the PIT-derived rate diverges >±12.5% from the TSC-derived rate, the TSC value is used (plausibility clamp). Safe PIT fallback when the TSC is unavailable, so single-timer real HW is never bricked. **IMPORTANT reconciliation:** the 300s "wedge" in the diagnosis row was **host-load/TCG starvation under concurrent agents, not a kernel bug** — on a quiet KVM host the `-smp 2` DE image boots in ~4s. | **DIAGNOSIS: `newshell hostowner` 30–60s / `enter linux` 2s = an SMP wedge, not startup cost (2026-07-01)** | User reported these commands are slow on the live desktop. Profiled on the real `hamnix-installer.img` under OVMF/KVM with wall-clock serial timestamps. On `-smp 1` BOTH are sub-second (`newshell hostowner` +0.4s incl. password; `enter linux` +0.4s cold / +1.0s warm) — the newshell/enter code paths have **no** startup inefficiency. On `-smp>1` the whole guest stalls/wedges during the runlevel-5 fork+exec app-launch storm (~15 DE apps): `-smp 2` boot 300s+ then hard-wedge; timestamped run showed 1234 serial lines in ~12.5s then **187.5s of total silence (clock included)** — a true wedge. Both `newshell` and `enter` are fork+exec, so on multicore they hit this contended path → the user's 30–60s. Two measured factors: (1) **LAPIC timer miscalibration under KVM** — PIT-anchored `lapic_calibrate_and_setup_timer()` (`arch/x86/kernel/apic.ad`) reports 100Hz but jiffies advance ~18–30× too fast → per-CPU IRQ storm; (2) a scheduler/IPC deadlock exposed by the concurrent fork+exec storm. The global `_execve_lock` (`f404c73c`) was neutralized+rebuilt+re-tested → wedge PERSISTED → **ruled out**. Incidental: the live serial console already runs as regular user `live` (uid 1001). | **Diagnosis (no code change — SMP timer/scheduler fixes are high-risk on real HW; documented per brief).** Fix tracked (task #7): re-anchor LAPIC calibration to TSC/HPET with a plausibility clamp; add an SMP-boot CI gate for the full DE image (current `-smp 2` CI is `-kernel`/cpio only and survives, missing this). Relates to `#413` steal-window race + the known pipe-SMP-hang. |
| **Interactive-QA sweep: 3 real bugs + 2 broken gates (2026-07-08)** | Drove the shipped `hamnix-installer.img` under UEFI/OVMF over serial with a marker-bracketed probe battery. **(1) Installer image would not build at all** — `build_installer_img.sh` pinned `HAMNIX_ROOTFS_SIZE_MB=512`, overriding `build_rootfs_img.py`'s auto-sizer, while the Debian fixture closure grew to 555 MiB staged → `mkfs.ext4: Could not allocate block`. Now auto-sizes with a 512 MiB floor (`106b9ebb`). Nothing in CI builds the shipped image, which is why it hid. **(2) `/proc/{mounts,stat,diskstats}` never returned EOF** — `devmounts_read`/`devstat_read`/`devdiskstats_read` ignored the file offset and always re-rendered from byte 0, so `read()` never returned 0. `df` (a read-to-EOF loop) spun forever and, as the foreground job, took the serial console with it: 25 of 33 probes never executed. `namec.ad:_devtab_read` already threads `off` into `devfirewall_read` for exactly this reason — it was dropped for these three siblings (`09c26399`). An audit of every `DEV_*` snapshot leaf confirms all others carry an `if off > 0: return 0` guard, so the fix is complete, not a sample. **(3) `uptime` reported uptime/100** — two `/proc/uptime` renderers disagree on units; the bound backend (`#c/uptime`) is Linux-shaped seconds, the legacy `fs/procfs.ad` arm is centiseconds (`5c2d9a08`). **(4) `test_mm_pressure.sh` could never boot** — it staged the whole debootstrap Debian closure into the kernel ELF (337 MiB) then booted `-m 256M`, so GRUB died `out of memory`; every marker went missing and all 12 assertions reported hard FAIL. Fixed with `HAMNIX_DEFAULT_REAL_DEBIAN=0` (kernel → 46 MiB), KVM when available, and INCONCLUSIVE-on-zero-markers (`2b34b273`). **(5) `test_pipe.sh` is a false green** — it greps serial for a payload a broken pipe leaks to that same console. | **#471 apt-NX VMA fault: straddling-alias MAP_FIXED replace (2026-07-08)** | `_vma_drop_overlapping_aliases` dropped only FULLY-CONTAINED pure aliases on a `MAP_FIXED` re-overlay. An alias that merely straddled the new range survived, and because the interval-tree stab returns the greatest-start cover, a right-straddling stale alias (`lo <= s0 < hi < e0`) won the boundary page — a demand fault then stamped the leaf PTE with the stale node's prot/backing (NX-onto-exec, or wrong file bytes). Whether an alias straddles or is enclosed depends on the random mmap slide, which is exactly why the apt "Reading package lists" crash was ASLR-flaky. FIX: trim any overlapping pure alias to its non-overlapping remainder(s), preserving prot/flags/fd and advancing `file_offset` on the right remainder. | **Done (gate-verified)** — `test_mm_pressure.sh` E7b `[mm] PASS: vma straddling-alias MAP_FIXED replace`. A differential run (`mm/vma.ad` reverted to `09c26399` vs the fix, same gate) shows the change introduces **zero** new failures and fixes exactly its own assertion. (merge `890bcb8c`) |
| **`ls /bin` was silently empty — shadow tmpfs overlay roots opened as 0-byte FILES (2026-07-08)** | Found by driving the shipped image: `ls /bin` printed nothing and exited 0, though 231 binaries live there and the whole DE execs from it. `fs/vfs_mount.ad` registers eleven top-level names (`/usr /etc /bin /sbin /lib /lib64 /opt /run /srv /var /tmp`) as shadow **tmpfs overlay roots** so apt/dpkg get a writable layer over the read-only initramfs. `vfs_open`'s tmpfs arm only asked `tmpfs_path_exists()` before taking the FILE arm, so `open("/bin")` returned a readable **zero-byte tmpfs file fd**; `p9_listdir` read 0 bytes and `ls` faithfully printed an empty directory. `fs/cpio.ad` was NOT at fault — `_cpio_listdir` always synthesized directories from the flat archive correctly, and only the eleven overlay *roots* were broken (nested `/lib/modules`, `/usr/share/man` always worked). `ls /usr/bin` erroring was likewise CORRECT: that directory does not exist (`/usr` holds only `share`). FIX: `_cpio_listdir_at()` appends the cpio prefix-scan after the tmpfs entries and dedups (tmpfs wins, it is the shadowing writable layer); `_dir_xform_lookup_meta` falls through to cpio metadata on a tmpfs miss (all 228 `/bin` binaries had reported size 0, and hamfm drew file icons on folders); cpio implicit dirs report `QTDIR`. Incidental: `0755`/`0644` were **decimal** literals — 755 decimal is `0o1363`, low bits `0o363`, which is why `ls -l /lib` rendered `d-wxrw--wx`. | **Done (image-verified, revert-proven)** — `scripts/test_ls_overlay_dirs.sh` asserts specific names (`/bin` >=100 incl `hamsh`/`ls`/`cat`; `/etc` incl `motd`/`passwd`; `/lib` incl implicit dir `modules`; `/lib/modules` incl `e1000e.ko`; `ls -l /lib` marks `modules` QTDIR). Reverting `fs/vfs.ad` and rebuilding gives exit 1 with `/bin` at 0 entries; restored gives exit 0 with `/bin` = 228. NOT fixed on purpose: `lsblk: cannot list /dev/blk` is `etc/users/default.ns` doing `unmount /dev/blk` for non-hostowner sessions per `docs/security.md` Phase 9 — re-binding would undo a security boundary. Residual wart: `#c`'s `_dev_listdir` hardcodes `blk` into `ls /dev`, so a stripped namespace names a path it cannot open (own commit). (merge `a37d9efb`) |
| **mm self-test range collided with the live mmap window (2026-07-08)** | With `test_mm_pressure.sh` resurrected, 7 assertions failed. None were memory-manager bugs. `vma_tree_selftest` built its probe VMAs at `BASE = 0x200000000`, which **is** `VMA_LARGE_BASE` verbatim — the first address `_vma_win_alloc` hands out — while its own comment claimed "far above any real mapping". It sat on top of the PART A/C demand VMAs `mm_pressure_selftest` had just allocated: gap probes resolved to those real VMAs (`gapmiss=6`), and teardown's `start >= BASE` filter deleted the self-test's own VMAs (`leftover=4`). Moved the range above `VMA_LARGE_LIMIT` (16 GiB / 16.25 GiB) and added a pre-flight range-clear probe that fails loudly if it ever stops being virgin. Separately, `fault-in populates the LRU` failed only because the gate grepped the literal `"32 pages"` while the kernel printed `88` — the kernel assertion (`>= 32`) was passing. The 56-page residue is the boot tasks' COW-shared anon pages (`mapcount > 1`), which `page_is_anon` correctly refuses to evict (evicting one sharer's PTE would strand the other). Replaced with an exact **delta** assertion (`== 32`), which is stronger than the old `>=`. | **Done (gate green)** — `test_mm_pressure.sh` exit 0, 28 `[mm] PASS` markers, 26/26 checks. `teardown removed 264` (was 266 — exactly the two VMAs it was wrongly eating). | **ext4 open-table exhaustion was reported as ENOENT — a present file 'did not exist' (2026-07-08)** | `fs/ext4.ad` had ONE GLOBAL **8-entry** open-file table, and `ext4_open()` returned the same `-1` for "no such file" and "table full". `fs/vfs.ad:_open_ext4_read` laundered that `-1` into **ENOENT**. So the **9th concurrently-open ext4 file anywhere on the box** — and every one after it — told userspace a file that exists does not exist. The overflow `printk` was INFO-level, so the console loglevel gate swallowed it and the failure was silent. FIX: `EXT4_MAX_OPEN` 8 -> 512; a distinct `EXT4_OPEN_EMFILE` mapped to `-EMFILE` so exhaustion is never confused with absence; exhaustion `printk` stamped EMERG; permanent concurrent-open / high-water-mark accounting; and `ext4_close()` now bounds-checks its slot, which it never did. | **Done** — probe goes from 8 simultaneous opens (9th => ENOENT) to **61** (now bounded by `_VFS_NR_FDS = 64`), and the new HWM line fires. Found while chasing the Firefox hang; **honest scope note: the HWM line never fires during a Firefox boot, so Firefox never crossed 8 — this is NOT Firefox's blocker.** It is a general correctness fix for every Linux-namespace app. (merge `4d26e10d`, `fa500806`) |
| **Firefox hang localized: a lost Pango GAsyncQueue handoff, NOT a futex/transport bug (2026-07-08)** | Symbolicated against staged libxul dbgsym + glib/pango debuginfod, reproduced across two independent runs. The long-standing "no FUTEX_WAKE is ever issued" framing is **WRONG** — the main thread's syscall ring shows `202 => 0` repeatedly, so it IS being woken; its predicate is never satisfied. Main thread parks in `pango_fc_fontset_get_font_at` (pangofc-fontmap.c:1193, `while (!pats->match && !pats->fontset) g_cond_wait(...)`); Pango's fontconfig worker (`fc_thread_func`, :992) sits in `g_async_queue_pop` -> `g_cond_wait` with an **EMPTY queue**. With `FC_DEBUG=17` in the guest, `FcInit()` completes and finds both DejaVu fonts but **no `Best score` / `Sort` line ever prints**, so `FcFontSetMatch()`/`FcFontSetSort()` never run: the `FC_MATCH` work item pushed by `pango_fc_patterns_new` (:1045) is never dequeued. Named anomaly for the fix: the worker task sits in `sc_nr=202` (futex) yet is **absent from the 6-entry futex wait table** — impossible for `_u_futex`'s bounded-park path. A 6-entry table for a 12-42-thread process is itself suspect, and explains why `foot`/weston (2-4 threads, poll-yield path) never hit it. DISPROVEN: COW-unshared thread memory, namespace thread I/O, FcInit from main+worker threads, Debian-version alignment, futex-key mismatch, GPU-probe child, AF_UNIX ring size, single-process mode. | **Diagnosis** — Firefox still reaches only ladder rung (a) (registry advertised); no buffer commit, no window. `test_wayland_phase4_term.sh` PASS (PNG viewed: weston-terminal renders text, typed `ls` echoes). Fix in flight. |
| **hamsh pipelines never carried a byte — and the gate that 'proved' they did was a false green (2026-07-08)** | Found by driving the shipped image: `seq 1 5 | wc -l` printed `1 2 3 4 5` (the LHS wrote to the CONSOLE) instead of `5`, and `ls /bin | wc -l` printed `0`. **Two defects.** (1) `run_one_command_x`'s builtin arm dispatched the verb in-process and returned **before any pipe wiring** — and `echo` is a builtin, which is exactly the command `test_pipe.sh` used to 'verify' pipes. (2) For externals the parent bound the child's `/fd/N` **after** `spawn()`; the code's comment claimed the child was still `STATE_READY` so the binds would land first — **false on SMP**: under KVM the child `execve`s and writes before the bind arrives, leaving `/fd/1` the COW-inherited console. **TCG always let the parent win, so no `-kernel` test ever saw it.** (3) Refcounts weren't held across the launch window — a probe write from a fresh stage returned `-32` (EPIPE) because nothing held the read end yet. FIX: `_run_builtin_in_pipeline` forks builtin stages (POSIX subshell semantics) and yields a **PID**; new `lib/p9.ad::spawn_pipeline_stage` binds pipe ends **child-side before execve** (no post-spawn parent bind); the shell **pins** each end at a scratch `/fd` name before forking, plus a rolling read pin in `run_pipeline`. The 'hamsh hangs after both children exit' half was the builtin arm returning an **exit status where `run_pipeline` stores a PID** — a builtin exiting `1` made the shell `sys_waitpid(1)`, a blocking wait on **init**, which never exits. | **Done (gate-verified, revert-proven)** — `test_pipe.sh` PASS (`seq 1000 1041 | wc -l` -> 42; `echo BUILTINPIPE | wc -c` -> 12; 3-stage -> 19; redirect; dup; shell survives) and `test_multipipe.sh` PASS. Each case now asserts the consumer's **computed answer** (a count no producer prints, so a leak cannot fake it) **AND** the absence of producer output on the console. Replaying the captured pre-fix transcript through the new assertions FAILs; the old substring grep matches that same broken transcript and would report PASS. Sibling false-greens fixed: `test_multipipe.sh` (which also matched the command being *typed*) and `test_hamsh_fdbind.sh`'s two pipe checks. **CAVEAT: both gates temporarily default to `-smp 1`** (`HAMNIX_TEST_SMP` overrides) because the pre-existing `yield_to_others` scheduler stall wedges the shell after ANY pipeline at `-smp 2`; flip back once that lands. (merge `f38348bd`) |
| **The large-thread-group FUTEX_WAIT park was INFINITE, not bounded — killed every heavily-threaded Linux app (2026-07-08)** | For thread groups above `FUTEX_BLOCK_THRESH` (6), `FUTEX_WAIT` took a blocking park advertised as self-healing: `wq_wait_commit_timeout(&futex_wq, FUTEX_PARK_TICKS)`, "re-read *uaddr every ~30 ms". **That re-evaluation never ran.** The deadline is only checked by the parked task's own loop, which continues solely while `_another_task_ready()==0` (the `sti;hlt` idle arm). The instant any other task is runnable the parker calls `schedule()`, goes `STATE_WAIT`, and `_pick_next` never re-selects a `STATE_WAIT` task — there is no timer wheel. So on any busy box the 'bounded' park is infinite. glibc/musl/cairo/pango mutate futex words WITHOUT issuing FUTEX_WAKE (glibc elides the wake when no waiter is registered), so any thread that parks in that window is dead for the life of the process. Second, independent bug: slot claim/release ran WITHOUT `_futex_lock` (the lock FUTEX_WAKE takes), so two claimers overwrite each other's registration and a bare `futex_addr[su]=0` on exit clobbers a re-claimed slot — the waiter is parked in sc_nr=202 yet invisible to FUTEX_WAKE, which zero-matches and evaporates. Both are thread-group-size-gated, which is exactly why foot/weston/Qt (2-4 threads, poll-yield arm) rendered and Firefox (12-42 threads, blocking arm) hung in Pango's GAsyncQueue GCond. FIX: all slot claim/release goes through ownership-checked helpers under `_futex_lock`; each bounded parker records a deadline in `futex_deadline[]` and a new `_futex_sweep_expired()` directed-wakes any elapsed parker, published to the arch timer as `linux_futex_tick_hook` (same Layer-2->arch inversion as `vdso_tick_hook`) and also run on SYS_futex entry; IRQ-safe (`spinlock_trylock`, `_futex_nparked` short-circuit). `FUTEX_BLOCK_THRESH` and the wait-strategy gating are untouched (weston/cairo need the poll-yield cadence). | **Done (gate-verified, revert-proven)** — new `test_futex_elided_wake.sh`: 8 spinners keep the box runnable so the parker can never service its own deadline, one thread parks in an untimed FUTEX_WAIT, main mutates the word with no FUTEX_WAKE -> `U-FUTEX: PASS`. Proven revert-sensitive: without the tick hook the same test HANGS (`[parked-wd] slot=17 sc_nr=202`, no verdict). `test_u28_musl_thread_many` PASS (counter=8000). General fix for every threaded Linux binary. Firefox's failure mode CHANGED — it no longer wedges: completes FcInit/font-matching, runs GTK to GtkHeaderBar/MozillaGtkWidget style resolution, all 23 threads present in the wait table (named anomaly gone), then sits in a normal idle event loop without creating a wl_surface. Still ladder rung (a) only; remaining gap is new + non-futex, between GTK realize and wl_compositor.create_surface. (merge `7c86b066`) |
| **The `-smp 2` guest wedge — a SINGLE GLOBAL time-slice counter shared across CPUs (2026-07-08)** | Long recorded as "unreproducible on quiet KVM, parked pending a real repro". Given a 70 s one-command repro this session (`-smp 1` idle shell ticks its heartbeat; `-smp 2` reaches stage-08 then goes TOTALLY SILENT, clock line included), then root-caused: `quantum_left` (the scheduler time-slice counter, `kernel/sched/core.ad`) was a **single global shared by every CPU**. `preempt_tick()` decrements it per BSP tick and preempts at 0, but `schedule()` AND the AP idle-loop dispatch re-arm it to a full slice on every dispatch — so a busy AP re-armed the shared counter tens of thousands of times/sec, far faster than the BSP's 100 Hz tick could drain it. The BSP's task therefore NEVER preempted, `hamsh` sat `STATE_READY` on `rq_head[0]` forever, and because CPU0 never context-switched it never reported an RCU quiescent state → grace periods stalled → the callback pool bled dry (the downstream "RCU stall" was a SYMPTOM, not the cause). Invisible at `-smp 1` (no second dispatcher). **NOT #413** — an `on_cpu` dump at wedge time showed every `STATE_READY` task `on_cpu==0` and only the `STATE_RUNNING` task `on_cpu==1`, so the steal-window handshake on main is correct. `_execve_lock` and LAPIC miscalibration were already ruled out. FIX: make `quantum_left` `Percpu[uint64]`; the AP idle-loop dispatch arms its own slice (+34 lines, deadlock-free). | **Done (gate-verified, revert-proven)** — heartbeats (KVM, `-smp 2`) 0 → 233-236 over 5 consecutive runs, no wedge. `test_hamsh_heartbeat.sh` gained an `-smp 1` CONTROL arm: `-smp 1` lives + `-smp 2` empty ⇒ demonstrable SMP wedge ⇒ FAIL (was INCONCLUSIVE — which is how this hid for weeks); neither lives ⇒ INCONCLUSIVE. Reverting the one line makes the gate FAIL. `test_mm_pressure.sh` PASS; `test_smp_de_runlevel5.sh` (full DE, `-smp 2`, OVMF) PASS. Follow-ups (tasks): AP periodic tick for `-smp>=3` blocked on a futex-sweep hard-IRQ lock-ordering AB-BA; a pre-existing `-smp 3/4` AP-launch trap. (merge `b804a4b8`) |
| **Test-suite health: ~600 dead -kernel gates unblocked + wait4 ECHILD fix + 32 dead accessors removed (2026-07-09)** | Three fixes from a cleanup campaign, verified coexisting on the shipped image. (1) **~600 `-kernel` unit gates were green on CI but red on any dev host that ran debootstrap:** `build_initramfs.py` defaults `HAMNIX_DEFAULT_REAL_DEBIAN=1`, linking the ~305 MiB debootstrap closure into the kernel ELF (~334 MiB), so GRUB OOMs loading it at the gates' `-m 256M` before the kernel runs — the fixture is gitignored so fixtureless CI (46 MiB busybox kernel) stayed green. | **The `-smp 2` fork+wait wedge — a one-line recursive rq-lock self-deadlock (2026-07-09)** | The SECOND, distinct `-smp 2` wedge (the idle-shell one was `quantum_left`, `4ef4a2da`): at `-smp 2` the shell hard-froze after ANY foreground external command — even a single `/bin/echo` on its own line wedged the next line (both vCPUs pegged 100%). NOT the suspected `yield_to_others`/#413 race (that framing was disproven). Root cause: `schedule()` takes `_rq_lock_cpu(my_cpu)` at the top; when the BSP finds no local work, nothing pullable, AND the current task is an EXITED zombie, it fell into `while True: _rq_lock_cpu(my_cpu)` **without releasing the outer hold** → cpu0 spins forever on a lock it already owns. The AP branch released first; the BSP branch did not. Trigger: a foreground external child exits on the BSP while its parent (yielding in `sys_waitpid_jc`) was work-stolen onto the AP → cpu0's rq empty → the dead child's `task_exit_current → schedule()` hits the bug. Lock-free probe: `RQLOCK-STUCK cpu=0 wants rq[0] owner=1`. **FIX = one line: `_rq_unlock_cpu(my_cpu)` before the BSP idle-loop.** | **Done (full battery, revert-proven)** — new gate `test_smp2_foreground_external.sh` (two back-to-back externals at `-smp 2`): removed the line → FAIL WEDGE (both vCPUs 100%); restored → PASS. | **9P write/create through a mount returned EPERM — the cpio read-only policy swallowed mounted paths (2026-07-09)** | Core Plan 9 correctness bug (found by the test-suite sweep): after `mount`ing a 9P/served path, READ through it worked but the FIRST write/create returned a clean `permission denied`. Root cause = the SERVER-side kernel-local perm gate, not the transport: `chan_permission_check`'s "everything else under `/`" fallback (`vfs_fs_kind → FS_KIND_CPIO`) mis-attributed a path under a `mount()`ed 9P server to the cpio (`#r`) root, whose write policy categorically denies writes (baked read-only). The READ leg passed because cpio *defers* reads of files it doesn't hold (`idx<0` → grant) — producing the exact READ-OK / WRITE-EPERM asymmetry; the 9P mount was simply invisible to the perm gate. FIX (`fs/vfs.ad`, 25 lines): at the top of `chan_permission_check`, recognise a path under a `CHAN_KIND_SRV` mount via the existing `chan_find_srv_prefix()` (the same lookup the READ path already uses) and grant at the kernel boundary, deferring the permission decision to the mounted server — correct Plan 9 semantics (the server enforces its own mode bits on Topen/Tcreate/Twrite; a genuinely read-only mount still rejects on the wire). No local-server policy changed. | **Done (verified, enforcement intact)** — `test_perm_servers` PASS (per-server perm enforcement byte-identical — the change is surgical, an early grant only for 9P-SRV-mount paths). Fix proven by substantive assertions: `test_9p_realfd` full create→write=13→reopen→read byte-exact round-trip through the mount, `test_9p_concurrency` creates+300-iter read loops (both were a clean EPERM without the fix). `test_p9mount`/`test_p9wstat` regressions PASS. The two fix gates reach INCONCLUSIVE only from starved distrofs teardown on this degraded host (add to CI on a quiet host). Secondary `do_stat(/etc/motd)` = -1 split to its own task (real, unrelated, not shipped). (merge `a7eeb7b8`) |
| **`stat()` returned -1 for every cpio-baked file under a writable overlay (/etc /bin /usr /var /lib) (2026-07-09)** | `stat("/etc/motd")` → -1 (so `ls -l /etc`, `stat /bin/ls` all failed), even though `open("/etc/motd")` worked. Same overlay-shadow family as the earlier `ls /bin`-empty bug. Root cause: `vfs_fs_kind`'s longest-prefix match over the `vfs_mount` table routes a path under a writable-overlay dir (e.g. `vfs_mount("/etc", FS_KIND_TMPFS, shadow=1)`) to `_stat_hook_tmpfs`, which returned -1 on a tmpfs miss **without honoring the mount's `shadow=1` fall-through to the cpio base** — while the read/open path (`vfs_fs_shadow`) DOES fall through, producing the exact open-OK / stat-FAIL asymmetry. (Disproved a prior 'resolves onto the ext4 sysroot' hypothesis: the fixture boots cpio-only, so `bind '#sysroot' /` never happens.) FIX (`sys/src/9/port/sysfile.ad`, `fs/vfs.ad`): `_stat_hook_tmpfs` defers to `_stat_hook_cpio` on a shadow-mount miss (mirroring the read path; non-shadow `/tmp` stays authoritative); `_stat_hook_cpio` emits a `QTDIR` record for implicit cpio dirs (flat archive) via a stable FNV `_cpio_dir_qid`. | **Done (verified, revert-anchored)** — `test_p9file` PASS (`stat /etc/motd ok` + general stat/fstat/create/remove green), added to CI as the overlay-fall-through regression anchor. `test_ls_overlay_dirs` PASS (the sibling overlay family — `/bin` >=100 entries, `/etc` incl `motd`, QTDIR dirs intact — no regression), `test_ext4` PASS. Root-caused via static trace (no boot-time diagnostic left behind). (merge `e218c404`) |
| **distrofs 9P daemon hung at teardown — a spawn'd server leaked the launcher's pipe write-fd (2026-07-10)** | `distrofs` (the userland 9P daemon serving the Debian namespace) completed every op — version/attach/walk/create/write/read/stat — then hung at teardown: the client's `waitpid()` blocked on a daemon that never exited. NOT a 9P framing/length desync (the codec is self-framing; a daemon trace showed the final `Rclunk` was sent `rc=0`) and NOT timing (deterministic under KVM). Root cause: `spawn` uses rfork `RFFDG` (child gets a private COPY of the whole fd table) then `dup2`s the transport pipe ends onto fd0/fd1 — but the child also holds a live copy of `c2s_wfd`, the **write end of its own stdin pipe**, which `dup2` never closes. So the c2s pipe's writer-count stays >0 forever, the daemon's fd0 read never sees EOF when the client closes its end, and it blocks in `_read_exact`. FIX (`user/distrofs.ad`): `closefrom(3)` at `main()` entry — drop every inherited fd above stderr (a 9P server opens its backing by name, needs nothing ≥3). | **Done (verified, revert-proven)** — `test_distrofs` FAIL→PASS (`[distrofs] EOF, exiting` → `PASS`; the unfixed traced run hangs = revert-proof), wired into CI. `test_distrofs_persist` PASS. Live path intact: `enter linux { /bin/ls }` reaches distro files (no ENOENT, lists `bin/`) with the fix. **CLASS finding (task):** the same RFFDG fd-leak affects other spawn'd-server fixtures (`test_p9srv_demo`, …) — the systemic fix is a spawn-layer clean-fd-table contract (closefrom after dup2'ing 0/1/2). Found by the evidence-directed test sweep. (merge `3bd0f01c`) |
| **Track 4 — UMDF: stock `.ko` runs in a restartable USERLAND host, out of the kernel fault domain (2026-06-20)** | First vertical slice of "drivers as restartable userland file servers." A user-mode driver is a normal CPL3 process: `user/umdf_host.ad` ports the ET_REL loader (ELF64 parse, SHF_ALLOC layout, x86_64 relocation, symbol resolution, `init_module` dispatch) into userland — the `.ko` loads into `mmap`'d USER memory and runs `init_module` in ring 3. Three **privileged kernel primitives** are exposed over a narrow syscall channel (`linux_abi/umdf_kernel.ad`, hooks in `arch/x86/kernel/syscall.ad` so Layer 1 never names Layer 2): **MMIO map** (`SYS_UMDF_MMIO_MAP` 321 — uncacheable phys→user-VA overlay), **DMA alloc** (`SYS_UMDF_DMA_ALLOC` 322 — phys-contiguous pages mapped to user VA with the phys exposed for device programming), **IRQ file** (`SYS_UMDF_IRQ_OPEN` 323 + a blocking `read` on the returned irq fd — per-vector `WaitQueue` woken by a per-row IRQ trampoline). The driver posts a `#umdf` server (namespace law). **Crash isolation**: a per-task hook (`register_umdf_task_exit_hook`, called from `task_exit_current`) reclaims IRQ files + DMA buffers on clean exit AND on crash; MMIO/DMA overlays are marked `VmaNode.is_foreign` so teardown clears the PTEs without `free_page()`ing device/DMA frames. Two supporting root-cause fixes: (a) `do_page_fault` now delivers **SIGSEGV** on an unmapped USER fault instead of halting the box (a NULL deref in any userland process — incl. a buggy vendor `.ko` host — no longer panics the kernel); (b) `VmaNode.is_foreign` free-path arm. | **Done (VM-verified)** — `scripts/test_umdf_host.sh`: a hermetic stock-shape probe `.ko` (built from tracked `m2_string.ad` via the Adder `x86_64-linux-kernel-module` target + `as`, no Linux tree) loads + `init_module`s IN USERLAND (`MODULE INITIALIZED IN USERLAND`), `DMA PRIMITIVE OK` (real `dma phys=0x08cdc000`), `IRQ PRIMITIVE OK`, then a host `crashme` (NULL deref) → kernel SURVIVES (`UMDF-KERNEL-SURVIVED-CRASH`) → a fresh host re-inits (restartability). `qemu rc=124` slow-host timeout judged by serial content. In-kernel loader path unchanged + still available. FOLLOW-UPs (tracked in TODO): respawn supervisor (auto-restart), real BAR-backed driver, userland-shim parity with `exports.ad`, and an rc-line `argv[2]` hamsh quirk (selftests default DMA/IRQ args). See `docs/umdf.md`. |

| **Linux-ABI syscall selftest sweep: 3 hidden EFAULT/EINVAL bugs — a missing uaccess_kernel bracket class (2026-07-10)** | Migrating 9 in-boot Linux-ABI syscall selftests (`close_range`, `memfd`, `pidfd`, `pidfd_getfd`, `fhandle`, `statx_getrandom`, `mqueue`, `splice`, `copy_file_range`) onto the three-valued `verdict_boot_gate` surfaced **3 real, deterministic, previously-hidden kernel bugs** — one root-cause class at three call sites in `init/main.ad`. A `boot:37.*` selftest runs the FULL syscall handler, whose `copy_*_user`/`strncpy_from_user` operate on the selftest's KERNEL-mapped (US=0) buffers, but the gate invoked the selftest **without** the `uaccess_kernel_begin/end` bracket its siblings (`close_range`/`splice`) use — so uaccess's strict US-bit check rejected the kernel page. **fhandle**: `name_to_handle_at` → `-EFAULT` deterministically. **statx_getrandom**: `getrandom` → `-EFAULT`. **mqueue**: `mq_open` → `-EINVAL` (the name `copy_from_user` failure was masked into `_mq_validate_name`'s zeroed-scratch leading-`/` check, surfacing as -22 not -14). The migration (assert the genuine kernel `[tag] PASS` OUTPUT banner, no serial input → no input-echo false-green class) is what exposed them. | **Done (image-verified, revert-anchored)** — all 3 proven FAIL→PASS with deterministic repros + clean second boot; independently re-run on merge (`[fhandle] PASS`, `[mqueue] PASS`, `[STATX_GETRANDOM] PASS`, rc=0 each). All 9 gates added to `scripts/ci_battery_manifest.txt` (the round-robin-sharded battery), so they run on every push. The other 6 gates passed as-is (already bracketed or bypassing uaccess). | **/dev + srv selftest sweep: `test_devmapper` never passed — a bcache-above-dm-remap test gap (2026-07-10)** | Second evidence-directed sweep batch (12 gates migrated onto the three-valued verdict: `pipe_chan`, `devfd_chan`, `devstat_split`, `devnet_local`, `devmouse_write`, `devmapper`, `fd_marker_uniqueness` in-boot; `dup`, `srv_post`, `srvtest`, `devdiskstats`, `dev_namespace` serial-driven onto `_hamsh_drive.sh`). This is FAITHFUL cache behaviour matching Linux — the dm targets are CORRECT. **Fix at the correct layer (the selftest):** `bcache_invalidate_all()` (a helper whose docstring exists precisely for this) before each target-routed read; NO dm target logic changed. | **ext4 selftest sweep: a deterministic AHCI-root boot double-fault + verdict-helper hardening (2026-07-10)** | Third evidence-directed sweep batch — 16 ext4 gates (the installed root FS, high-stakes) migrated onto the three-valued `verdict_boot_gate` (in-boot selftests assert the kernel `[ext4*] PASS` banner; `test_ext4`/`_fsync`/`_inline` driven serial via `_hamsh_drive.sh`). 15 PASS; the migration exposed **1 real, deterministic kernel bug**. **`test_ext4_dirrename` — an AHCI-root boot #DF:** it is the ONLY ext4 gate that boots off an `ich9-ahci`/`ide-hd` disk (the rest use virtio-blk, all green); the boot reaches `[ahci] NCQ block-path ENABLED (FPDMA QUEUED, IRQ-driven)` then dies `TRAP: vector 0x08 err=0xa1 rip=0x8` (#DF) with an early `[pa-corrupt] page scribbled while free (UAF/double-free)`, BEFORE the ext4 selftest runs — so it emitted zero markers and the old MISS→hard-FAIL tail hid it as indistinguishable-from-host-load. | **AHCI-root boot double-fault fixed — a sleep-before-`sched_init()` ordering bug (2026-07-10)** | The deterministic #DF surfaced by the ext4 sweep (booting off `ich9-ahci`/`ide-hd` dies `TRAP: vector 0x08 rip=0x8` right after `[ahci] NCQ block-path ENABLED`) is root-caused and fixed. **The UAF framing was DISPROVEN:** the `[pa-corrupt] page scribbled while free` line is a deliberate self-healing `[pa-stress]` corruption-injection self-test firing ~130 ticks earlier — a red herring. Real cause: the AHCI NCQ FPDMA block path (`_ncq_block_rw_sync → wq_wait_commit_timeout → schedule()`) **SLEEPS on a wait queue, but is first exercised by the rootfs `blk_read` on an AHCI boot (`init/main.ad` ~4547) BEFORE `sched_init()` runs (boot:37, ~6396)** — a blocking wait before the boot task's CR3/weight/run-lists are published switches into an uninitialised task context and jumps to a near-null RIP (#DF) or deadlocks (timing-sensitive: printks flipped one face into the other). virtio-blk boots stayed green because only the AHCI path routes early reads through a sleeping completion path. **Fix (correct layer = the driver's path selector):** `sched_init()` sets a one-shot `_sched_up`; new `sched_is_up()` exposes it; `_ahci_block_path_active()` gates on it and falls back to the legacy POLLED path (`_do_*_lba`, already validated by `ahci_smoke_test`) until the scheduler is live — after which NCQ FPDMA + IRQ completion activate exactly as before. | **Done (image-verified, revert-anchored)** — differential-verified on the merged tree: `test_ext4_dirrename` FAIL→PASS (#DF gone), and critically `test_ahci_ncq_blkpath` PASS (NCQ FPDMA + IRQ completion + multi-slot concurrency still route through the fast path post-`sched_init` — the fix is a pre-scheduler fallback, not a disable), `test_ahci` PASS. Gate re-added to `ci_battery_manifest.txt` (90 gates). New invariant recorded in memory. (merge `5a2ae400`) |
| **Block/storage selftest sweep: getrusage -EFAULT (7 selftests) fixed + NCQ cold-path deadlock found (2026-07-10)** | Fourth sweep batch (11 AHCI/blk gates migrated onto the three-valued verdict; 7 added to the manifest). Two real bugs. **(1) FIXED — `getrusage` -EFAULT:** `_u_getrusage` (linux_abi/u_syscalls.ad) was converted to assemble `struct rusage` in a kernel scratch and `copy_to_user` it — correct for real user callers, but `copy_to_user` rightly refuses a KERNEL-address destination (US=0 → -EFAULT), so the SEVEN in-kernel accounting selftests (rusage/pgfault/ctxsw/blkio/nsignals/vmstat/ruchild) that hand it their own kernel buffer all silently returned -EFAULT (`[BLKIO] FAIL getrusage rc=…602`). None were gated, so it was invisible. Fix: factored the field-assembly into a shared `_getrusage_fill(who, kru)`; `_u_getrusage` fills a kernel scratch then copy_to_users it (byte-identical for real callers), and the selftests fill their own kernel buffer directly. **(2) FOUND (held out, own task) — NCQ cold sleeping-path deadlock:** driving `_ncq_block_rw_sync` COLD (first blk_read/write after sched_init, no prior busy-poll warmup) wedges forever — the AHCI completion IRQ never wakes the `wq_wait_commit_timeout` sleeper AND the jiffies-deadline fallback never fires. NOT device-specific (disproved the ich9 hypothesis — hangs on generic `-device ahci` too); distinct from the boot #DF (#31 was sleeping BEFORE sched_init; this is the post-sched_init sleeping path). The merged `test_ahci_ncq_blkpath` misses it because its FPDMA assertions busy-poll (warm the port) before the trailing blk_read. Held out: test_ahci_blk/_recovery, test_blk_sched. | **Done (image-verified, revert-anchored)** — differential-verified on the merged tree: the REAL user-facing `test_rusage` still PASSes (shared refactor byte-identical for real callers — no regression), `test_blkio` FAIL→PASS (the fix target), a new AHCI gate `test_ahci_write` PASS. 7 storage gates registered in `ci_battery_manifest.txt` (97 gates now). NCQ cold-path deadlock tracked as an open task. (merge `9bb7c9d3`) |
| **NCQ cold sleeping-path deadlock fixed — AHCI GHC.IE (global interrupt enable) was never set (2026-07-10)** | The NCQ cold-path deadlock (from the storage sweep) is root-caused and fixed. The AHCI driver set `GHC.AE` (AHCI Enable) but **never `GHC.IE`** — the GLOBAL Interrupt Enable gate (AHCI spec §3.1.2). With it clear the HBA suppresses every port's `PxIE`-armed source and never asserts its INTx line, so `ahci_irq_handler` never ran (`irq_count=0`) and the cold NCQ FPDMA sleeper (`_ncq_block_rw_sync → wq_wait_commit_timeout`) had NO waker. The jiffies-deadline timeout backstop couldn't rescue it either: `get_jiffies()` is frozen (~7) during the IF=0-heavy native boot (the LAPIC tick barely fires pre-userland), so the deadline never held. No waker + dead timeout = permanent hang. **The lost-wakeup-race framing was DISPROVEN:** the completion was already latched (`PxIS=9`, `HBA_IS=1`) — the HBA was globally gated from ever raising the line (`GHC=0x80000000`: AE set, IE clear; `irq_count=0`). Warm gates survived because `test_ahci_ncq_blkpath` busy-polls `_ncq_irq_complete_port` to drain, needing neither IRQ nor timeout. **Fix (correct AHCI layer):** set `GHC.IE` (read-modify-write, keeping `GHC.AE`) immediately after the IRQ handler is registered and the IOAPIC pin routed, so the first asserted interrupt lands on a live handler — one constant + two lines; the NCQ FPDMA fast path stays genuinely IRQ-driven. | **Done (image-verified, revert-anchored)** — after the fix `GHC=0x80000002`, `irq_count=1`, the sleeper woke via a real IRQ data-wake (`rc=0`, not a timeout/poll-downgrade), confirmed under KVM AND TCG. Independently re-verified on the merged tree: `test_ahci_blk`, `test_blk_sched`, `test_ahci_recovery` all FAIL/hang→PASS; warm-path `test_ahci_ncq_blkpath` PASS (no interrupt storm). All 3 re-added to `ci_battery_manifest.txt` (100 gates now). Boot-time-timeout gotcha recorded in memory. (merge `c395c746`) |
