Six big rocks fanned out in parallel; the headline is that **adversarial verification paid off — half were already implemented and the agents found real LATENT BUGS in them instead**, plus a precise architectural diagnosis on the hardest. **Shipped:** (1) **MDS** — `VERW`/CLEAR_CPU_BUFFERS on all 8 kernel→user exit sites (4 SYSRET unconditional, 4 IRETQ-to-kernel RPL-gated), MDS active=1, no triple-fault; reuses the existing Spectre-v2 md_clear probe. (2) **TLS** — DISPROVED "build a TLS client": a 5,511-line in-kernel TLS 1.3 stack (drivers/net/tls.ad: X25519, AES-GCM/ChaCha20, RSA-PSS/ECDSA, X.509 chain validation) already existed; the real gap was a redirect guard blocking `http→https` (13-line fix, on-device verified). (3) **X.509 real chains** — the genuine HTTPS blocker: the parser rejected real chains; added PKCS#1 v1.5 sha256/384/512-RSA + a DigiCert G2 anchor → **4 real public chains validate** (Let's Encrypt/ISRG, debian.org, digicert.com, microsoft.com). (4) **apt install** (endgame keystone) — DISPROVED "forked-worker reloc" (already fixed by #471); real bug was `dup`/`dup2`/`dup3` never propagating `O_NONBLOCK`, so a recycled fd slot's stale nonblock bit made dpkg's `tar` read(0) EAGAIN-abort on the 2nd package; fixed → a dependency pair installs end-to-end (both "Setting up", postinst, dep-ordered, binary runs). (5) **RCU** — DISPROVED "no RCU" (a full quiescent-state RCU exists in kernel/rcu/rcu.ad); found + fixed a **latent use-after-reap** (`task_lookup_by_pid` resolving STATE_REAPING zombies → `kill(pid)` resurrects a dead mapping) + a rotted/un-gated RCU gate. (6) **KPTI** — DISPROVED the swapgs-less-%gs deferral reason; the real wall is that `PML4[0]` is simultaneously the kernel direct map AND the user-page backing, so a protective user CR3 can't hide the heap without relocating the direct map to a high-half `page_offset` first; landed the boot-safe scaffold (Meltdown detection, user-CR3 constructor, trampoline primitives w/ VERW ordering, a passing isolation selftest, gated OFF) + filed the mm follow-up (#94). | **Done — MDS/TLS/X.509/apt/RCU shipped + fresh-image/host verified + pushed; KPTI scaffold shipped + gated + diagnosis, live-isolation = #94.** Every merge on a clean build with the evidence in hand; stale-base agent collisions reconciled (MDS/RCU rebased); kernel-parity memory corrected (RCU is done). Verification discipline caught confounded `-smp 2` MDS heartbeats under concurrent-agent load (deferred to a quiet re-check, tied to #55). |
| **KVM real-HW-fidelity probe + native-kernel unblock + SVG/compiler fixes (2026-07-12)** | Kernel lane reopened after the #100 native-link fix, plus a new real-HW-fidelity verification capability. **Shipped, each fresh-image verified:** (#100) **native-kernel link ship-blocker** — `elf_emit.ad` now emits public module globals as STB_GLOBAL so `idt_table` (from cpu_entry_area asm) resolves; before this every kernel gate silently fell back to the Python SEED compiler, so the default/shipped kernel had NOT actually been native-built; confirmed the native kernel both links (new `test_native_kernel_links.sh` guard) AND boots healthy. (#99) **DE apps-no-render** — launch-queue apps now create windows (`window N mapped pid=` on-boot, screendump-confirmed). (#101/#103) **SVG rasterizer** — from-scratch integer SVG (shapes + path M/L/H/V/C/Q/Z + arcs A/a + smooth S/T + rounded rects; Q16 integer trig via `_sdiv` to dodge a compiler bug); fixed a latent 256×-too-thin stroke-width bug. (#102) **compiler signed div/mod** — DISPROVED the "pow2 missing sign-bias" framing: the pow2 lowering was already correct; the real defect was signedness *detection* — a signed `/` or `%` with a COMPUTED dividend (`(a*x - b*y)`) resolved type shallowly, fell back to unsigned, and emitted `divq`/logical `shr` (`-4003/1024`→~2^54); fixed in both backends (native `codegen.ad` + seed `codegen_x86.py`) by resolving operand signedness structurally through binops; `%` was affected identically; differential fuzzer 500/500 + 0 miscompiles. (#104) **page-alloc boot-selftest strand** — `page_alloc_stress_test()`'s DESTRUCTIVE corruption-injection ran on EVERY shipped boot; the allocator's (correct) self-heal truncates the order-0 free list, stranding memory a later ELF load could bogus-`elf: OOM` on under a real-HW memory layout; split the destructive half into a marker-gated `page_alloc_corrupt_inject_test()` (precedent: the ext4 `g_*_test` gates) + added a net-neutral-free-count assertion as a permanent boot-path regression guard. **New capability:** opt-in `QEMU_ACCEL=kvm` on the installer-boot gate (default TCG so CI is unchanged) — a fast deadline-proof local boot AND a real-HW-fidelity probe; it immediately earned its keep by exposing the #104 strand class that pure TCG masks. | **Done — #99/#100/#101/#102/#103/#104 + KVM knob merged (through `474c2455`) and pushed**, each fresh-image / differential-fuzzer / host-gate verified by the orchestrator before push. Two orchestration hazards recorded to memory (parallel worktrees share the repo stash-stack/refs → `git stash`/`reset --hard` collide → ban stash in agents; leak-check the COMMIT not the stale-branch diff). Follow-ups: re-verify KPTI bricks natively + land Brick B (#94, in flight), a KVM real-HW-fidelity QA sweep (in flight), #55 intermittent -smp2 heartbeat (no #104 correlation established). |
| **Real-HW SMP + memory-reclaim + bind-safety batch, driven by a KVM fidelity probe (2026-07-12)** | A KVM (`-cpu host` ≈ real silicon) QA sweep — a new opt-in `QEMU_ACCEL=kvm` capability — surfaced a chain of real-hardware bugs that pure-TCG dev boots had masked, all fixed + fresh-image verified. (#105) **ACPI MADT enumeration returned 0 on every UEFI boot** — `acpi_find_rsdp()` scanned only the legacy BIOS window, which under OVMF/real-HW holds no RSDP (UEFI advertises it via an EFI config-table entry); so SMP fell back to an accidental APIC-ID-1 probe → **capped at 2 cores + single-IOAPIC assumption on any real machine**. Fixed by discovering the RSDP through the EFI config table the stub already hands over (non-UEFI falls through to the unchanged legacy scan) → real CPU + IOAPIC enumeration, correct interrupt routing. (#106) **native app-spawn leaked + OOM-wedged the boot** — the ELF64 region reclaim pool keyed regions by EXACT byte size so a freed 16.79 MiB region couldn't satisfy a 16.97 MiB request (21/27 allocs cold-missed the one-way memblock cursor, draining 568 MiB → OOM); and the execve-OOM print dereferenced the raw USER path pointer AFTER `vma_clear` unmapped it → printk `%s` kernel-#PF wedged the CPU mid-print. Fixed with an address-sorted coalescing first-fit-with-split reclaim list + logging the kernel path copy and returning -ENOMEM (per-app OOM now degrades gracefully; 640M–1G all boot). (#86) **`bind` onto a non-resolving source silently no-op'd** — `ns_walk` resolved the source to its covering server (`/`→`#r` covers everything) not an actual file; fixed with a syscall-layer existence probe that admits legit unprobeable sources (ext4/FAT/9P/`#`-spec) and hard-fails only a genuinely unbound source. **Self-caught regression:** #105's correct enumeration would bring up all cores on a 3-4-core box → the known-hard #12/#13 AP-scheduler trap (`rip=0xffffffff0000001c`) hard-kills the VM where the accidental 2-core cap previously booted; added `SMP_BOOT_MAX_CPUS=2` (enumerate all, START 2, park the rest) so real-HW multicore still boots — verified `-smp 4` enumerates 4, brings up 2, reaches `[hamsh-alive]`, no crash. Also re-verified KPTI bricks step1/A on the NATIVE kernel (were seed-only pre-#100) + landed KPTI #94 Brick B[1/4]+[2/4] (kstack + %gs onto the page_offset alias), stopping cleanly before [3/4] (needs `virt_to_phys` page_offset-aware + a 33-site DMA audit). | **Done — #105/#106/#86 + SMP cap + KPTI Brick B merged (through `6edd5c53`) and pushed**, each fresh-image / KVM-boot verified by the orchestrator (`RSDP via EFI config table`, `MADT reports N CPU(s)`, graceful `-ENOMEM`, rc.* `#distro` binds intact, `bringing up 2 (rest parked, see #13)`). Open follow-ups: #13 (AP-scheduler trap — the blocker to raising the SMP cap, in flight), #55 (intermittent -smp 2 heartbeat — #106 graceful-OOM likely resolves the wedge class), the DE working-set is large enough that ~5 apps OOM at -smp2/1G (a footprint follow-up, not a wedge). The KVM fidelity probe earned its keep: it found #104/#105/#106 that TCG never showed. |
| **SMP fully unblocked: -smp 2 preemption + AP scheduler races fixed, cap 2→8 (2026-07-12)** | Closed the entire SMP arc in one push, each fix statistically/both-accelerator verified. (#55) **-smp 2 idle-shell wedge** — DISPROVED "intermittent": deterministic 10/10. An AP is tickless (BSP owns the shared hrtimer) and the one-shot preemption backstop is never re-armed once the AP dispatches a real user task, so a CPU-bound DE app on an AP takes no timer IRQs, `preempt_tick` never runs, it monopolizes the core and starves the serial shell → no `[hamsh-alive]`. Fix (`arch/x86/kernel/time.ad`, 44 lines): re-arm the AP one-shot every tick after EOI (idle stays tickless); drive `jiffies` BSP-only so N busy APs don't run the clock N× fast (uptime verified ~1s/real-s). P(empty) 10/10→0/14; the heartbeat gate now sees 99 ticks (was 0). (#13) **-smp 3 AP-launch trap** — DISPROVED the `rip=0xffffffff0000001c`/futex-lock-ordering framing: a parked AP idle kthread left LINKED on a run-list was work-stolen and double-run on one kstack → stack corruption. Fix: unlink the parked idle kthread under the rq lock; cap 2→3. (#12/#413) **-smp 4+ steal-window** — DISPROVED the `on_cpu`-fence-hole framing (the fence held): TWO bugs — the AP idle kthread was `AFFINITY_ALL` (stealable once it yields → run with a stale cpu-id), and the AP idle loop dispatched at IF=1 so the newly-periodic #55 tick / a reschedule IPI re-entered `schedule()` on the idle stack. Fixes: pin each AP idle kthread to its own CPU + `local_irq_disable()` in the dispatch window; cap 3→8. Verified `-smp 1..8` clean to a live shell on KVM `-cpu host` AND TCG, `-smp 16` all online. New gates `test_smp3.sh`/`test_smp8.sh` (fail pre-fix, pass post-fix). Elegant causal chain: #105 (real enumeration) UNMASKED the >2-core bugs, and #55 (AP tick) SURFACED the #12 IF=1 window — each fix exposed the next. | **Done — #55/#13/#12 merged (through `46edd5b5`) and pushed**, orchestrator re-verified every gate on fresh images (test_smp8 all-7-APs-online + shell + heartbeat + no trap; test_smp3 isolated PASS; test_hamsh_heartbeat -smp2 97 ticks; uptime cadence sane). Hamnix went from 2 cores (an accidental UEFI-enumeration-failure fallback) at session start to a verified 8-core cap. Remaining: raise 8→16 needs a >12-core host to TCG-verify; the SMP-race lessons are in `project_smp2_idle_wedge` + `project_smp_realhw_madt`. |
| **SMP scales to a verified 64-core ceiling + hamsh becomes Python-esque (2026-07-12)** | Two arcs. **SMP → 64 cores:** #107 grew MAX_CPUS + all six lockstep per-CPU siblings (NR_RQ/AP_MAX_CPUS/ACPI_MAX_CPUS/TK_MAX_CPUS/NR_TSS_CPUS) 16→64 (drift-guarded); a broad KVM QA sweep then found the last blocker — an intermittent (~1/4) AP-idle-loop dispatch panic at -smp 8 (#109). **#109 DISPROVED the orchestrator's `%gs`-reads-0 lead** (all APs printed correct cpu-ids; the `cpu=0` was a symptom of an already-smashed kstack): the real cause was a residual of the #12/#13 steal window — `sched_prepare_ap_idle`→`kthread_create` published the AP idle kthread STATE_READY+LINKED+AFFINITY_ALL and only THEN pinned/parked/unlinked it, so in that gap a running AP work-stole cpu-N's not-yet-adopted idle kthread → two CPUs on one kstack. Fix: `kthread_create_parked_pinned()` publishes it parked+pinned+unlinked ATOMICALLY. Verified 14/14 (+orchestrator 2/2) -smp 8 clean, 4/4 -smp 12, no -smp 1/2/3 regression → **SMP_BOOT_MAX_CPUS raised to the full 64** (64 = the uint64-bitmask ceiling). `test_smp8.sh` now multi-boots + hard-fails on the panic banner. **hamsh → Python-esque scripting whose stdlib is Plan 9:** #110 added comprehensions (list+dict), tuples + unpacking (`a,b=1,2`, `for k,v in d.items()`, multi-return), slicing (`xs[a:b:c]`, `s[::-1]`, negatives), and the data builtins (`range/enumerate/zip/sorted/reversed/sum/min/max/len/abs` + `str/int/list/dict` + method-call desugar `d.items()`); #111 added the DIFFERENTIATOR — `with bind(SRC,DST): …` context managers that apply in-process and UNBIND unconditionally on every exit path (normal/error/unwind), `with enter(NS)`/`with mount(...)`, iterable+introspectable namespaces (`for m in $ns`, `binds(ns)`), and fixed the #110 nested-list render. All held to a differential "indent-form ≡ brace-form" proof; both fixed latent bugs along the way (`${ expr }`-with-spaces rendered empty; nested-list-literal pool). | **Done — #107/#109 (SMP) + #110/#111 (hamsh) merged (through `0a2f1566`) and pushed**, each gate-verified in a quiet window by the orchestrator (SMP: my own multi-boot -smp 8 clean + native-link; hamsh: differential dual-syntax gate + the `with`-bind namespace round-trip proving bound-inside/unbound-after). | **Overnight push, wave 5: foundational pivot — compiler, kernel-fault root-cause, modern JS runtime (2026-07-13)** | With the host-verifiable coreutils/browser surface saturated, the cycle pivoted to the harder frontier. **Compiler:** (#183) fixed a real LATENT miscompile — a module-level `float64` global with an initializer (`g: float64 = 1.5`) hard-errored in the seed but SILENTLY emitted 0.0 in the native backend (a value-level miscompile invisible to objdiff — the reason 3+ agents this session resorted to fixed-point). | **Overnight push, wave 6: #112 FIXED, modern JS runtime + SPA/canvas browser, hamsh exceptions (2026-07-13)** | The session's kernel arc CLOSED and the browser reached real-web-engine capability. **#112 FIXED (#184→#189→#191, three passes, two framings disproved):** the intermittent `-smp 2` user SIGSEGV was root-caused NOT as an SMP race but as `do_execve` OOM past the point-of-no-return under MEMORY PRESSURE (it tore down a fork-child's COW image PTEs, then the eager contiguous `region_alloc` OOMed on a large binary → child resumed into unmapped code). Proven by `-m256M`→1/8 vs `-m1G`→0/12 and a live PTE-clear→SIGSEGV log correlation. FIX (`fc0f7f75`): pre-check the image fits BEFORE teardown → clean `-ENOMEM` with the caller intact (Linux execve semantics), + deterministic kill past the PONR instead of resuming unmapped. Verified fault 1/8→0/8 at -m256M, `precheck_aborts=0` across 3 -m2G DE boots reaching userland (zero false rejections), fork+exec -smp2 PASS, native_kernel_links PASS. | **★ KPTI ship-path security fix + continued push (2026-07-14, USER: "keep pushing, and fix the security bug")** | **THE SECURITY FIX (#94, `5ca263bc`):** driving the shipped installer image (QA-by-using) surfaced that KPTI Brick A — the cpu_entry_area (CEA) that keeps the entry structures mapped in the user CR3 — was INCOMPLETE on the UEFI/installer boot (the actual ship vehicle) though the `-kernel` gate `test_kpti.sh` reported PASS (a textbook `feedback_real_boot_path_testing` false-green). Instrumentation DISPROVED the orchestrator's UEFI-timing hypothesis: the real bug was the CEA window was a SINGLE PD linked at `PDPT[0]` covering only the first 1 GiB from `.text`, and `_cea_map_page` dropped the `>>30` PDPT bits — so any entry structure ≥1 GiB from `.text` mapped into the wrong PD slot AND aliased an unallocated PDPT entry. On `-kernel` the small image keeps everything <1 GiB (passes); on the shipped installer the large embedded rootfs bloats `.data`, pushing the `.bss` IDT/GDT/TSS/#DF past 1 GiB while `.rodata` VERW + `.text` stay under — exactly the observed `IDT=0 GDT=0 TSS=0 DF=0 VERW=1 text=1`. FIX: replaced the fixed single-PD scheme with a lazy multi-level CEA mapper (`_cea_walk_child`) that derives pdpt/pd/pt indices from the CEA VA and allocates a PD per touched 1 GiB + PT per 2 MiB, spanning the whole image; plus the previously-unchecked `_cea_map_range` returns. VERIFIED on BOTH paths (orchestrator independently re-booted the fixed image): `-kernel` test_kpti PASS; UEFI installer under OVMF now prints `cpu_entry_area walk: IDT=1 GDT=1 TSS=1 DF-stack=1 VERW=1 entry.text=1 → cpu_entry_area PASS`; native_kernel_links PASS; a synthetic +1.25 GiB probe repro 0→mapped. See `project_kpti_cea_uefi_divergence`. **Continued push (disjoint, same session):** hambrowse Grid round 8 (#249, `09e1d635`) — `grid-column` span + explicit placement + `grid-template-rows` fixed heights; DE modern polish round 2 (#251, `2f98399b`) — headerbar elevation hairlines, softened Control-Center nav rail, near-white panel popup menus (looked at the render). Also on-device-verified the whole wave-9 DE-modern refresh by booting the shipped image (indigo-slate wallpaper + accent titlebar render on the real compositor). | **Done — #94/#249/#251 merged + pushed (through `2f98399b`)**, the security fix triple-verified (both boot paths + native link + synthetic probe), the browser + DE rounds host-gate + render verified. Reward-disproof paid off hard: the orchestrator's own "cosmetic wording" and "UEFI-timing" framings were both overturned by evidence — the real bug was a 1 GiB CEA-window ceiling. Follow-ups filed: #248 (harden test_kpti.sh with a UEFI-boot arm so this false-green class can't recur), #250 (hambrowse `_prop_is` newline handling). |
